eld-companies?tags=22735"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=22735"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=22735"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":449557049,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/united-states\/","name":"United States","slug":"united-states","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449557049"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449557049"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449557049"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449557049"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449557049"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2321284,"date":"2022-05-18T14:37:26","date_gmt":"2022-05-18T21:37:26","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2321284"},"modified":"2022-05-19T16:46:21","modified_gmt":"2022-05-19T23:46:21","slug":"usdtea-more-stable-than-bitcoin-crypto-stablecoin-arizona-iced-tea","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/18\/usdtea-more-stable-than-bitcoin-crypto-stablecoin-arizona-iced-tea\/","title":{"rendered":"What’s more stable than Bitcoin or UST? AriZona Iced Tea"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">ICYMI, stablecoins are in deep shit right now, and the chaos that unfolded this week has thrown the entire crypto ecosystem into turmoil with over $400 billion in losses from just one coin alone. In these times of uncertainty, all we can rely on is that we can purchase a can of AriZona Iced Tea for 99 cents, the"https:\/\/www.latimes.com\/business\/story\/2022-04-12\/az-iced-tea-inflation-99-cents\">same price<\/a> that the refreshing beverage sold for in 1996.
"https:\/\/mossydotcom.com\/\">Mossy<\/a>, a collective of three techy artists, thinks that an (unofficially)"http:\/\/usdtea.io\">AriZona-backed stablecoin<\/a> can save the crypto economy.<\/p>\nA stablecoin, as the name implies, is supposed to be stable because it tracks the value of another asset \u2014 similar to how gold bars once backed the U.S. dollar during gold-standard times.<\/p>\nIn the case of TerraUSD (UST), formerly one of the largest stablecoins that fell from grace this week, each UST coin was supposed to stay consistently equivalent in value to one U.S. dollar. But there were no physical reserves \u2014 instead, the group behind UST used algorithms and reserves of other cryptocurrencies to manage its price. That system"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/12\/binance-halts-luna-and-ust-trading-across-most-of-its-spot-pairs-following-meltdown\/\">went haywire<\/a>, leading some holders of UST to withdraw their money, and before investors knew what had hit them, the panic and fear compounded and UST was trading as low as"https:\/\/www.cnbc.com\/2022\/05\/16\/what-happened-to-the-bitcoin-reserve-behind-terras-ust-stablecoin.html\">nine cents on the dollar<\/a>. UST\u2019s sudden collapse has led to over $400 billion in losses for investors over the past week or so,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/terras-ust-crash-will-make-life-harder-for-crypto-as-regulation-looms\/\">leaving people to question<\/a> the, well,stability<\/i> of stablecoins as a whole.<\/p>\nMossy\u2019s solution for the calamitous sector,"https:\/\/usdtea.io\/\">a stablecoin called USDTea<\/a>, is backed by what they claim is America\u2019s most stable asset: cans of AriZona Iced Tea. For over 30 years, AriZona founder Don Vultaggio"https:\/\/www.latimes.com\/business\/story\/2022-04-12\/az-iced-tea-inflation-99-cents\">has been working tirelessly against inflation<\/a> to keep the cost of each can at exactly 99 cents, playing hardball with suppliers to keep input costs low and sacrificing his own profit for the sake of consistency.<\/p>\nAs for Mossy, you may have seen their work before. The group launched the \u201c"https:\/\/nfog.xyz\/\">Non-fungible Olive Gardens<\/a>\u201d project that got them in"https:\/\/www.businessofbusiness.com\/articles\/opinion-non-fungible-olive-gardens-NFTs-started-off-as-a-joke-but-heres-why-the-project-has-serious-implications-for-business\/\">some hot water over copyright laws<\/a> as well as the \u201c"https:\/\/theblockedchain.xyz\/\">Blockedchain<\/a>\u201d NFTs that only Twitter users who have been blocked by famed (and pugnacious) venture capitalist Marc Andreessen can mint.<\/p>\nMossy quietly announced the"https:\/\/usdtea.io\/\">USDTea stablecoin project<\/a> on Twitter one and a half hours before selling out all 1,000 tokens they initially supplied. We sat down with"https:\/\/brianmoore.com\/\">Brian Moore<\/a>, one of the three members of the artists\u2019 collective \u2014 another member is Mike Lacher, who recently went viral for his AI that"https:\/\/www.mikelacher.com\/work\/how-bad-is-your-spotify\/\">harshly judges<\/a> your music taste, while the third member chooses to remain anonymous. Moore regaled us with his (mostly) straight-faced, highly serious explanation of Mossy\u2019s ambitions to bring stability to an unstable world \u2014 one can of iced tea at a time.<\/p>\n"attachment_2321310\" style=\"width: 1502px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2321310\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2321310 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-18-at-5.24.47-PM.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1492\" height=\"879\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-18-at-5.24.47-PM.png 1492w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-18-at-5.24.47-PM.png?resize=150,88 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-18-at-5.24.47-PM.png?resize=300,177 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-18-at-5.24.47-PM.png?resize=768,452 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-18-at-5.24.47-PM.png?resize=680,401 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-18-at-5.24.47-PM.png?resize=50,29 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1492px) 100vw, 1492px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2321310\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong>"https:\/\/usdtea.io\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">USDTea"screen-reader-text\">(opens in a new window)<\/span><\/a><\/p><\/div><\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nTC: So, who are you? What is this collective that tries to save crypto through AriZona Iced Tea?<\/strong><\/p>\nBM: We\u2019re a little group called Mossy, and the last three things we\u2019ve made have all been web3 projects. We created"https:\/\/nfog.xyz\/\">non-fungible Olive Gardens<\/a>, and then we did"https:\/\/theblockedchain.xyz\/\">Blockedchain<\/a>, which was an NFT series that you can only mint if you\u2019re blocked by specific people on Twitter, like Marc Andreesen. And now the latest is USDTea, which is a stablecoin that\u2019s linked to the most stable asset we know on planet Earth, which is AriZona Iced Tea.<\/p>\nCan you literally connect your wallet to this and get a token?\u00a0<\/strong><\/p>\nWell, first of all, I just got word that we are fully out of the 1,000 that we started with [after about an hour and a half post-launch]. That\u2019s the weirdness of this world. It was the same thing with non-fungible Olive Gardens; we quietly released it, and then it was gone within I think 10 hours.<\/p>\nAriZona Iced Tea might be $0.99, but what about gas fees?<\/strong><\/p>\nThe way the flow works is the fees aren\u2019t super high. It\u2019s an ERC 20 token. I bought some and I think it was, you know, negligible, like $4 or something in gas fees. And then, just like any other stablecoins that are pegged to currency, you can always switch back. In this case, you can burn your USDTea and we will ship you cans of AriZona Iced Tea, because it wouldn\u2019t be backed by it if we didn\u2019t actually do that. So we have our strategic reserves of AriZona Iced Tea to use if people want to convert it back at any given time.<\/p>\nDo you actually have 1,000 cans of tea?\u00a0<\/strong><\/p>\nIt\u2019s 1,000 cans where we\u2019re starting. That might expand in the future. And if we do that, I think we\u2019d probably be open to external auditing depending on the situation, but currently, we\u2019ve got 1,000 cans basically, and we will distribute them as necessary. Right now we do have reserves split around different locations around the U.S.<\/p>\nDo you make these satirical web3 projects as your full-time job?<\/strong><\/p>\nThe more we do this, the more it becomes something that is more full time, but I\u2019d say we\u2019re mostly artists.<\/p>\nHow many people are you?<\/strong><\/p>\nWe\u2019re three people. So we\u2019re pretty \u2026 I guess the word would be nimble. It allows us to make things very quickly. In the case of the destabilization of currency-pegged cryptocurrencies, you know, when did that whole snafu go down? We\u2019re trying to bolster the crypto economy as quickly as possible, and we can only do that with a small team.<\/p>\n"attachment_2321307\" style=\"width: 1840px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2321307\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2321307 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-18-at-5.08.03-PM.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1830\" height=\"1686\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-18-at-5.08.03-PM.png 1830w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-18-at-5.08.03-PM.png?resize=150,138 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-18-at-5.08.03-PM.png?resize=300,276 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-18-at-5.08.03-PM.png?resize=768,708 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-18-at-5.08.03-PM.png?resize=680,626 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-18-at-5.08.03-PM.png?resize=1536,1415 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-18-at-5.08.03-PM.png?resize=50,46 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1830px) 100vw, 1830px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2321307\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong>"https:\/\/usdtea.io\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">USDTea"screen-reader-text\">(opens in a new window)<\/span><\/a><\/p><\/div><\/p>\nDid you conceive of this idea last week when Terra was collapsing?<\/strong><\/p>\nExactly. There\u2019s something to be said about the stability of stablecoins, right? That\u2019s half the word, stable. And then you think, what\u2019s the most stable thing you can imagine? AriZona Iced Tea, you really can\u2019t beat it.<\/p>\nHow do you make money off of this, or is making money not the goal?\u00a0<\/strong><\/p>\nIt\u2019s not necessarily the goal, really, but I think we want to support ourselves at some point. We\u2019re in the interest of making interesting work on the internet, and that is the ultimate goal. If it makes us money, great, and if it doesn\u2019t, then that\u2019s fine too. Ultimately, we\u2019re just making interesting things \u2014 making people think, making people laugh, or, you know, stabilize their assets in canned iced teas.<\/p>\nHowwould<\/i> you make money?<\/strong><\/p>\nThese are fungible assets, so it\u2019s meant to be more of a currency replacement than, say, an individual art piece. One USDTea is equal to one USDTea. There\u2019s no one of them that\u2019s better than the other or rarer than the other. They\u2019re all equal to one can of AriZona\u2019s Iced Tea.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n"en\" dir=\"ltr\">AriZona stablecoin when??<\/p>\n— AriZona Iced Tea (@DrinkAriZona)"https:\/\/twitter.com\/DrinkAriZona\/status\/1526263719323258882?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">May 16, 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\nBut to redeem your can of tea, you have to pay a $20 flat processing fee. What is that fee?<\/strong><\/p>\nThat\u2019s just literally the logistics of shipping. That\u2019s not a money-making scheme to make profit off of the transaction; it\u2019s to get you your personalized tea assets that you can store in your own location.<\/p>\nOn your website, you have the question \u201cwhat happens when ETH crashes?\u201d, and you say that you update the ETH\/USDTea to match ETH\/USD from time to time. What does that entail?<\/strong><\/p>\nIt just means that as Ethereum might change in price, we want to match that so the rate ends up being around 99 cents.<\/p>\nHow often will you do that? I imagine you don\u2019t have an algorithm.<\/strong><\/p>\nNo, there\u2019s no algorithm yet. That might come in the future \u2014 it all depends on how wide we expand this. We\u2019re taking it one step at a time. This has been about 90 minutes worth of launch time, so once we stabilize our own situation, we\u2019ll figure out what we need to do.<\/p>\nObviously, Terra was the inspiration for this project. Do you have any opinions or takes about what happened, and how Terra\u2019s handling that?\u00a0<\/strong><\/p>\nI think our company speaks through the work itself. We\u2019re here to try to stabilize an unstable world, so I think that backing our assets in a new, innovative and most importantly stable asset \u2026 I think that sort of says all that we need to say about that situation.<\/p>\n"attachment_2321291\" style=\"width: 310px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\">"caption-attachment-2321291\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-medium wp-image-2321291\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/gettyimages-513289628-594x594-1.jpg?w=300\" alt=\"An anteater is pictured\" width=\"300\" height=\"203\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/gettyimages-513289628-594x594-1.jpg 594w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/gettyimages-513289628-594x594-1.jpg?resize=150,101 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/gettyimages-513289628-594x594-1.jpg?resize=300,203 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/gettyimages-513289628-594x594-1.jpg?resize=50,34 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2321291\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">An anteater.
Image Credits:<\/strong> MICHAL CIZEK\/AFP via Getty Images<\/em><\/p><\/div><\/p>\nWould you say you\u2019re bullish or bearish on crypto?\u00a0<\/strong><\/p>\nAre we bullish? Are we bearish? I don\u2019t know. I think we\u2019re exploring it. We love it as a medium through which to make interesting art pieces. I don\u2019t think we necessarily have an answer or have an animal to assign to it. You can just say anteater or something like that.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"i0it3N9WgY\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/terras-ust-crash-will-make-life-harder-for-crypto-as-regulation-looms\/\">Terra\u2019s UST crash will make life harder for crypto as regulation looms<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; Andreessen","slug":"marc-andreessen","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/1104174"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=1104174"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=1104174"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=1104174"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=1104174"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576612036,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/stablecoin\/","name":"stablecoin","slug":"stablecoin","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576612036"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576612036"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576612036"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576612036"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576612036"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2320989,"date":"2022-05-18T12:15:34","date_gmt":"2022-05-18T19:15:34","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2320989"},"modified":"2022-05-18T12:27:02","modified_gmt":"2022-05-18T19:27:02","slug":"grubhub-free-lunch-nyc-promo","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/18\/grubhub-free-lunch-nyc-promo\/","title":{"rendered":"Grubhub’s free lunch promo creates a literal ‘Hell’s Kitchen’ for NYC restaurants"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">Grubhub offered"https:\/\/twitter.com\/Grubhub\/status\/1526579510115803136\">free lunch<\/a> to everyone in New York City yesterday. What could go wrong?<\/p>\nBetween 11 a.m. and 2 p.m., New Yorkers could use a Grubhub promo code to get a $15 discount on lunch. Naturally, restaurants got flooded with an unexpected deluge of orders. According to"https:\/\/www.buzzfeednews.com\/article\/kelseyweekman\/grubhub-free-lunch-nyc-promo-chaos\">Buzzfeed<\/a>, a worker at a Mexican restaurant in Harlem hand-delivered orders herself via Uber, since their in-house delivery driver was too overloaded. An employee at Greenberg’s Bagels in Brooklyn also told Buzzfeed that they received 50 orders in an hour, whereas they typically receive about 10 orders from Grubhub per day.<\/p>\nAcross New York City, Grubhub said that it received about"https:\/\/www.axios.com\/2022\/05\/17\/grubhub-free-lunch-promo-new-york\">6,000 orders<\/a> per minute. Within an hour, some users tweeted that the promo code was no longer working, or that restaurants had marked themselves closed to avoid receiving any more orders. All in all, many orders got delayed and\/or cancelled, but restaurant workers and delivery drivers were most adversely impacted, struggling to fulfill orders at an impossible rate.<\/p>\nGrubhub said that it modeled this promotion after a previous one, but this time, customers used the promo code six times more, causing unexpectedly high demand.<\/p>\n“To help businesses prepare for yesterday\u2019s promotion, we gave advance notice to all restaurants in our network, which included multiple forms of communications across email and in-platform,” Grubhub said in a statement to TechCrunch. “Even with that preparation, no one could anticipate the level of demand and unfortunately that caused strain on some restaurants. We\u2019ll undoubtedly have a lot of learnings from this that can help us optimize and mitigate issues in the future.”<\/p>\nEvidently, many restaurant workers didn’t get the memo — and even so, taking proactive measures like adding an extra driver to a shift wouldn’t have prepared a restaurant to meet such a dramatic surge in demand.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n"en\" dir=\"ltr\">New Yorkers went as hard for free lunch as the Rangers did in game 7.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nOur restaurants and drivers are still working hard fulfilling your orders. Make sure to show them love today (and every day). \ud83c\udf55\ud83e\udde1<\/p>\n— Grubhub (@Grubhub)"https:\/\/twitter.com\/Grubhub\/status\/1526625528295440384?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">May 17, 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\nThis is not the first time that a Grubhub promotion inadvertently served restaurants the short end of the stick.<\/p>\nIn March, D.C. Attorney General Karl Racine"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/21\/grubhub-lawsuit-hidden-fees-dc-attorney-general-disclosure\/\">sued Grubhub<\/a> for \u201cmisleading District residents and taking advantage of local restaurants to boost its own profits.\u201d One incident the lawsuit referenced was Grubhub\u2019s early-pandemic-era \u201c"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/04\/05\/its-time-to-stop-using-grubhub-seamless-forever\/\">Supper for Support<\/a>\u201d promotion, which was discontinued. Launched in late March 2020, Grubhub offered restaurants the opportunity to offer a $10 coupon on orders over $30, but the restaurant had to foot the bill for that free food. On the consumer end, Grubhub encouraged customers to \u201csave while supporting the restaurants [they] love,\u201d even though their promotion actually put more strain on restaurants by pressuring them to lower profit margins.<\/p>\nFor yesterday’s promotion, Grubhub paid for customers’ $15 coupon, not the restaurants. The company says it fulfilled"https:\/\/www.axios.com\/2022\/05\/17\/grubhub-free-lunch-promo-new-york\">400,000 lunch orders<\/a>, which at $15 a pop, would put the company out $6,000,000 for what was largely a screw up.<\/p>\nGrubhub has also faced scrutiny and legal troubles for false advertising,"https:\/\/www.foodandwine.com\/news\/grubhub-class-action-lawsuit-adding-restaurants-without-permission\">listing restaurants on their app<\/a> without the business’ consent. That means that a consumer might place a Grubhub order for a restaurant that doesn’t know they’re even on Grubhub, meaning that the business could pay a fee to Grubhub without knowing it. Or, once a Grubhub courier arrives, the restaurant might not even know that they were expected to prepare that takeout order.<\/p>\nDespite an uptick in delivery orders during the pandemic, food delivery apps have still\u00a0"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/doordash-and-uber-eats-are-hot-theyre-still-not-making-money-11622194203\">struggled<\/a> to turn a profit. But customer acquisition promotions like yesterday’s likely won’t encourage customers to keep coming back to Grubhub.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"mjXad6j5M0\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/14\/food-delivery-profits-remain-elusive\/\">Food-delivery profits remain elusive<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“Food-delivery profits remain elusive” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/14\/food-delivery-profits-remain-elusive\/embed\/#?secret=ZyrPD55hEY#?secret=mjXad6j5M0\" data-secret=\"mjXad6j5M0\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"gluXi1wiSA\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/21\/grubhub-lawsuit-hidden-fees-dc-attorney-general-disclosure\/\">Lawsuit prompts Grubhub to add disclosures about hidden fees<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“Lawsuit prompts Grubhub to add disclosures about hidden fees” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/21\/grubhub-lawsuit-hidden-fees-dc-attorney-general-disclosure\/embed\/#?secret=hFIsGFvp4a#?secret=gluXi1wiSA\" data-secret=\"gluXi1wiSA\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"Grubhub offered free lunch to everyone in New York City yesterday. web","slug":"world-wide-web","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/2648"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=2648"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=2648"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=2648"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=2648"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2319807,"date":"2022-05-17T13:59:45","date_gmt":"2022-05-17T20:59:45","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2319807"},"modified":"2022-05-17T14:21:12","modified_gmt":"2022-05-17T21:21:12","slug":"buffalo-shooting-footage-facebook-twitter-moderation","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/buffalo-shooting-footage-facebook-twitter-moderation\/","title":{"rendered":"Facebook and Twitter still can\u2019t contain the Buffalo shooting video"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">Ten people were murdered this weekend in"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/16\/buffalo-mass-shooting-social-media\/\">a racist attack<\/a> on a Buffalo, New York supermarket. The eighteen-year-old white supremacist shooter livestreamed his attack on Twitch, the Amazon-owned video game streaming platform. Even though Twitch removed the video two minutes after the violence began, it was still too late — now, gruesome footage of the terrorist attack is openly circulating on platforms like Facebook and Twitter, even after the companies have vowed to take down the video.<\/p>\nOn Facebook, some users who flagged the video were notified that"https:\/\/twitter.com\/EoinHiggins_\/status\/1525860078166937601\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">the content did not violate its rules<\/a>. The company told TechCrunch that this was a mistake, adding that it has teams working around the clock to take down videos of the shooting, as well as links to the video hosted on other sites. Facebook said that it is also removing copies of the shooter’s racist screed and content that praises him.<\/p>\nBut when we searched a term as simple as “footage of buffalo shooting” on Facebook, one of the first results featured a 54-second screen recording of the terrorist’s footage. TechCrunch encountered the video an hour after it had been uploaded and reported it immediately. The video wasn’t taken down until three hours after posting, when it had already been viewed over a thousand times.<\/p>\nIn theory, this shouldn’t happen. A representative for Facebook told TechCrunch that it added multiple versions of the video, as well as the shooter’s racist writings, to a database of violating content, which helps the platform identify, remove and block such content. We asked Facebook about this particular incident, but they did not provide additional details.<\/p>\n"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">“We’re going to continue to learn, to refine our processes, to ensure that we can detect and take down violating content more quickly in the future,” Facebook integrity VP Guy Rosen said in response to a question about why the company struggled to remove copies of the video in an unrelated call on Tuesday.<\/span><\/p>\nReposts of the shooter’s stream were also easy to find on Twitter. In fact, when we typed “buffalo video” into the search bar, Twitter suggested searches like “buffalo video full video graphic,” “buffalo video leaked” and “buffalo video graphic.”<\/p>\n"attachment_2320128\" style=\"width: 479px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2320128\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2320128\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-17-at-8.58.45-AM.png?w=469\" alt=\"\" width=\"469\" height=\"288\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-17-at-8.58.45-AM.png 469w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-17-at-8.58.45-AM.png?resize=150,92 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-17-at-8.58.45-AM.png?resize=300,184 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-17-at-8.58.45-AM.png?resize=50,31 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 469px) 100vw, 469px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2320128\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> Twitter, screenshot by TechCrunch<\/p><\/div><\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nWe encountered multiple videos of the attack that have been circulating on Twitter for over two days. One such video had over 261,000 views when we reviewed it on Tuesday afternoon.<\/p>\nIn April, Twitter"https:\/\/help.twitter.com\/en\/rules-and-policies\/perpetrators-of-violent-attacks\">enacted a policy<\/a> that bans individual perpetrators of violent attacks from Twitter. Under this policy, the platform also reserves the right to take down multimedia related to attacks, as well as language from terrorist “manifestos.”<\/p>\n“We are removing videos and media related to the incident. In addition, we may remove Tweets disseminating the manifesto or other content produced by perpetrators,” a spokesperson from Twitter told TechCrunch. The company called this “hateful and discriminatory” content “harmful for society.”<\/p>\nTwitter also claims that some users are attempting to circumvent takedowns by uploading altered or manipulated content related to the attack.<\/p>\n"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">In contrast, video footage of the weekend’s tragedy was relatively difficult to find on YouTube. Basic search terms for the Buffalo shooting video mostly brought up coverage from mainstream news outlets. With the same search terms we used on Twitter and Facebook, we were able to identify a handful of YouTube videos with thumbnails of the shooting that were actually unrelated content once clicked through. On TikTok, TechCrunch identified some posts that directed users to websites where they could watch the video but didn’t find the actual footage on the app in our searches.<\/span><\/p>\nTwitch, Twitter and Facebook have stated that they are working with the Global Internet Forum to Counter Terrorism to limit the spread of the video. Twitch and Discord have also confirmed that they are working with government authorities that are investigating the situation. The shooter described his plans for the shooting in detail in a private Discord server prior to the attack.<\/p>\nAccording to documents reviewed by TechCrunch, the Buffalo shooter decided to broadcast his attack on Twitch because a 2019 anti-semitic shooting at Halle Synagogue remained live on Twitch for"https:\/\/www.cnbc.com\/2019\/10\/09\/the-german-synagogue-shooting-was-streamed-on-twitch.html\">over 30 minutes<\/a> before it was taken down. The shooter considered streaming to Facebook but opted not to use the platform because he thought users needed to be logged in to watch livestreams.<\/p>\nFacebook has also inadvertently hosted mass shootings that evaded algorithmic detection. The same year as the Halle Synagogue shooting, 50 people were killed in an"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/03\/21\/facebooks-ai-couldnt-spot-mass-murder\/\">Islamophobic attack<\/a> on two mosques in Christchurch, New Zealand, which"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/03\/18\/facebook-says-the-original-new-zealand-shooter-video-was-viewed-about-4000-times-before-removal\/\">streamed for 17 minutes<\/a>. At least"c-link\" tabindex=\"-1\" href=\"https:\/\/www.nytimes.com\/live\/2022\/05\/15\/nyregion\/shooting-buffalo-ny#the-2019-new-zealand-massacre-is-a-grisly-inspiration-for-racist-attacks\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https:\/\/www.nytimes.com\/live\/2022\/05\/15\/nyregion\/shooting-buffalo-ny#the-2019-new-zealand-massacre-is-a-grisly-inspiration-for-racist-attacks\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\" data-remove-tab-index=\"true\">three perpetrators<\/a> of mass shootings, including the suspect in Buffalo, have cited the livestreamed Christchurch massacre as a source of inspiration for their racist attacks.<\/p>\nFacebook noted the day after the Christchurch shootings that it had removed 1.5 million videos of the attack, 1.2 million of which were blocked upon upload. Of course, this begged the question of why Facebook was unable to immediately detect 300,000 of those videos, marking a"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/03\/17\/facebook-new-zealand\/\">20% failure rate<\/a>.<\/p>\n"font-weight: 400;\">Judging by how easy it was to locate videos of the Buffalo shooting on Facebook, it seems the platform still has a long way to go.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"AsEjbwXU7j\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/16\/buffalo-mass-shooting-social-media\/\">There are no easy answers for tech in the aftermath of the Buffalo tragedy<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“There are no easy answers for tech in the aftermath of the Buffalo tragedy” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/16\/buffalo-mass-shooting-social-media\/embed\/#?secret=SL1nbAtzh6#?secret=AsEjbwXU7j\" data-secret=\"AsEjbwXU7j\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"9rjL45H3OC\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/03\/21\/facebooks-ai-couldnt-spot-mass-murder\/\">Facebook’s AI couldn’t spot mass murder<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“Facebook’s AI couldn’t spot mass murder” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/03\/21\/facebooks-ai-couldnt-spot-mass-murder\/embed\/#?secret=536oUm6MhU#?secret=9rjL45H3OC\" data-secret=\"9rjL45H3OC\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"Ten people were murdered this weekend in a racist attack on a Buffalo, New York supermarket. senior Twitter employees leave amid potential Musk takeover"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\"> <\/p>\nAs Elon Musk tweets"https:\/\/twitter.com\/elonmusk\/status\/1526246899606601730\">poop emojis<\/a> at Twitter CEO Parag Agrawal, it appears that some of the platform’s executives are ready to move on.<\/p>\nAccording to a Bloomberg"https:\/\/www.bloomberg.com\/news\/articles\/2022-05-17\/twitter-loses-three-more-senior-employees-ahead-of-musk-takeover?sref=gni836kR\">report<\/a>, three senior employees are voluntarily leaving the company: Ilya Brown, a VP of product management for health, conversation and growth; Katrina Lane, VP of Twitter Service; and Max Schmeiser, head of data science. Per LinkedIn, Lane and Schmeiser had worked at Twitter for about one and two years respectively, while Brown had been at the company for six years.<\/p>\nTwitter confirmed these departures.<\/p>\n“We continue to be focused on providing the very best experience to the people on Twitter. We can confirm that they will be leaving Twitter for new opportunities. We are thankful for all of their hard work and leadership,” a spokesperson told TechCrunch.<\/p>\nThere’s been plenty of shakeups at Twitter’s senior level in recent weeks, and not just because of Musk’s"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/elon-musk-twitter-spam\/\">indecision<\/a> about his potential $44 billion purchase. Just last week, Agrawal"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/13\/twitter-ceo-tweets-musk-deal\/\">ousted two key executives<\/a>: revenue product lead Bruce Falck and head of product Kayvon Beykpour, who was on parental leave at the time. Beykpour said that Agrawal, who has been CEO for"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/29\/jack-reportedly-stepping-down-from-twitter-ceo-role\/\">under six months<\/a>,"https:\/\/twitter.com\/kayvz\/status\/1524787801757126656\">asked him to leave<\/a> because he wants to “take the team in a different direction.”<\/p>\nMusk has stated that if he does acquire Twitter, he would"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/29\/elon-musk-lined-up-twitter-ceo-ideas-monetizing-tweets\/\">install a new CEO<\/a>, meaning that Agrawal’s days in the role are numbered.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n“Some have been asking why a ‘lame-duck’ CEO would make these changes if we\u2019re getting acquired anyway,” Agrawal"https:\/\/twitter.com\/paraga\/status\/1525191760615329792\">wrote<\/a> on Twitter. “While I expect the deal to close, we need to be prepared for all scenarios and always do what\u2019s right for Twitter. I\u2019m accountable for leading and operating Twitter, and our job is to build a stronger Twitter every day.”<\/p>\nAt this point, Musk is dragging his feet on his acquisition of Twitter, claiming that the deal is “"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/elon-musk-twitter-spam\/\">on hold<\/a>” over the issue of spam bots.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"F08uM8nP0x\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/elon-musk-twitter-spam\/\">Musk says Twitter deal is dead unless CEO can prove spam stats<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“Musk says Twitter deal is dead unless CEO can prove spam stats” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/elon-musk-twitter-spam\/embed\/#?secret=b0I5wWdJqf#?secret=F08uM8nP0x\" data-secret=\"F08uM8nP0x\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"6XJsaOwfOR\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/13\/twitter-ceo-tweets-musk-deal\/\">Twitter CEO Parag Agrawal says he fired key execs due to ‘challenging’ economy<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“Twitter CEO Parag Agrawal says he fired key execs due to ‘challenging’ economy” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/13\/twitter-ceo-tweets-musk-deal\/embed\/#?secret=jqPi0lI43x#?secret=6XJsaOwfOR\" data-secret=\"6XJsaOwfOR\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"As Elon Musk tweets poop emojis at Twitter CEO Parag Agrawal, it appears that some of the platform’s executives are ready to move on. deal with Truth Social makes returning to Twitter complicated"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">These questions haunt us: Will Elon Musk’s bid to buy Twitter"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/13\/elon-musk-twitter-deal-on-hold-spam\/\">actually go through<\/a>? If so, will former President Donald Trump"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/10\/elon-musk-trump-perma-ban\/\">be allowed back<\/a> on the platform?<\/p>\nAccording to a new"https:\/\/www.sec.gov\/Archives\/edgar\/data\/0001849635\/000119312522150801\/d226205ds4.htm#rom226205_13\">filing<\/a> with the U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission regarding the Trump Media & Technology Group’s (TMTG) intention to"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/10\/21\/inside-the-trump-spac-deal-taking-on-twitter-disney-cnn-and-every-major-tech-company\/\">go public via SPAC<\/a>, Trump has some regulations to follow regarding the competition to his fledgling social network. Namely, when Trump posts a “truth” on Truth Social (yes, posts are called “truths”), he cannot repost it to any other social network for six hours.<\/p>\nThese restrictions are likely intended to drive traffic to Truth Social — the app’s daily active user counts pale in comparison to Twitter’s, and getting first dibs on Trump posts could be reason enough to onboard new users.<\/p>\nThe document also notes that “[Trump] may make a post from a personal account related to political messaging, political fundraising or get-out-the-vote efforts on any social media site at any time.” But he is “generally obligated” to use Truth Social.<\/p>\nIn any case, it’s in the former president’s best financial interest to sway users over to his app. Per this S-4 filing, he will own 46.8% of company voting power and 73.3 million shares of TMTG once it merges with the blank check company Digital World Acquisition Corp.<\/p>\nTrump was issued a permanent ban from Twitter in January 2021 for"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/08\/trump-banned-from-twitter\/\">inciting violence<\/a> when thousands of his supporters violently stormed the U.S. Capitol building. At the time, he had nearly 89 million followers on the platform, whereas currently on Truth Social, his “truths” reach 2.9 million people.<\/p>\nElon Musk"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/10\/elon-musk-trump-perma-ban\/\">has said<\/a> that if he does end up owning Twitter, he would want to unban Trump. But it’s unclear if Trump even wants to come back to Twitter — he says he doesn’t, but can he really"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/26\/why-trump-is-coming-back-to-twitter-sorry\/\">resist the temptation<\/a>?<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nSo far, Truth Social has had a rocky start in its mission to “rival the liberal media consortium.” In February, the app hit the top of the App Store charts, but"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/21\/trumps-truth-social-app-launch-store-errors\/\">few users<\/a> were actually able to join (we registered on February 21 and got off of the waitlist on April 23). Former Republican Congressman Devin Nunes, who is now CEO of TMTG, had promised the app would be “"https:\/\/www.theguardian.com\/us-news\/2022\/feb\/20\/trump-truth-social-app-fully-operational-march-devin-nunes\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">fully operational<\/a>” by the end of March, but the app remains in testing and is only available on iOS.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"TNXFbC9AsE\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/26\/why-trump-is-coming-back-to-twitter-sorry\/\">You know damn well that Trump is coming back to Twitter<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; Owl City remixed Smash Mouth’s ‘All Star’"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">My Chemical Romance yesterday released their"https:\/\/www.spin.com\/2022\/05\/my-chemical-romance-the-foundations-of-decay\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">first single since 2014<\/a>. Kendrick Lamar just dropped"https:\/\/pitchfork.com\/news\/kendrick-lamar-releases-new-album-mr-morale-and-the-big-steppers-listen\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a new album<\/a>. But did you know that this morning, Owl City"https:\/\/www.prnewswire.com\/news-releases\/smash-mouth-owl-city-break-the-mold-with-a-fresh-vibrant-reimagining-of-all-star-owl-city-remix-301545023.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">remixed<\/a> Smash Mouth’s seminal hit “All Star”?<\/p>\nYou might be wondering why we are covering this on TechCrunch, which is not a music website. My editor is probably wondering the same thing. But here are the tech angle(s):<\/p>\n\n“All Star” is to internet culture as “Jane Eyre” is to gothic literature. It’s a classic. Especially with the rise of TikTok, songs\u00a0are<\/em> memes now — be honest with yourself, did you know who Capone was before the “oh no no no” song went viral? How many Gen Z-ers listened to Fleetwood Mac for the first time because of the Ocean Spray longboarding guy? Smash Mouth would have faded from relevance much earlier if “All Star” didn’t appear in the opening sequence of “Shrek,” a film that has become inextricable from its second life on the internet.<\/li>\nLet’s not forget Owl City, the solo project ofelectronic<\/em> (tech angle!) musician Adam Young. The dude knows he’s a one-hit wonder, and he’s in on the joke. He wrote the lyric, “You would not believe your eyes\/if ten million fireflies\/lit up the world as I fell asleep,” then goes on to claim that he got “a thousand hugs from ten thousand lightning bugs.” Listen. I might be a writer who is shitposting about Smash Mouth on a Friday to distract herself from other things (uhh,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/13\/elon-musk-twitter-deal-on-hold-spam\/\">Elon Musk<\/a>), but Iam<\/em> a writer, and I’ll tell you, that lyric makes no fucking sense. But Owl City did what any butt of a joke on the internet had to do: he committed to the bit, cementing himself as anall star<\/em>. When a fan asked him what he meant by that lyric — “does each firefly hug you 1,000 times, or do only 1\/10th of the bugs give you a hug?” — Young wrote a"https:\/\/www.facebook.com\/owlcity\/posts\/10155050947042025:0\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">long Facebook post<\/a> (yes, Facebook, atech<\/em> company — tech angle!) confirming that he “was embraced 1,000 times by 10,000 luminescent insects.” Great stuff here.<\/li>\nJohn and Hank Green helped shape the creator economy as we know it — their business DFTBA Records fulfills merchandise purchases for a number of independent internet personalities, and they co-founded VidCon, an annual convention about online video. Not to mention that they helm one of the longest-running, large internet communities via their YouTube channel, vlogbrothers. Online video? Big deal. How many"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/12\/russia-ukraine-social-media-war-crimes-congress\/\">letters from Congress<\/a> have been written to TikTok recently?Tech angle<\/em>. But to bring things back to “All Star,” the two forty-something-year-old men spent several months over the course of 2020 only uploading YouTube videos titled with lyrics from “All Star.” It was kind of a"https:\/\/www.youtube.com\/watch?v=XMb9WP7NTqk\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">beautiful<\/a> project.<\/li>\nOwl City’s remix of “All Star” is only being distributed digitally. Is that a tech angle?<\/li>\n<\/ol>\nAnyway, if you want to distract yourself from the"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/13\/startup-tech-layoff-and-hiring-freeze-in-may\/\">doom and gloom<\/a> of tech, have you considered listening to Owl City’s remix of “All Star”? video","slug":"online-video","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/27908"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=27908"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=27908"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=27908"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=27908"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":234802,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/shrek\/","name":"shrek","slug":"shrek","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/234802"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=234802"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=234802"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=234802"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=234802"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2317855,"date":"2022-05-13T05:00:18","date_gmt":"2022-05-13T12:00:18","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2317855"},"modified":"2022-05-16T17:06:42","modified_gmt":"2022-05-17T00:06:42","slug":"startup-tech-layoff-and-hiring-freeze-in-may","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/13\/startup-tech-layoff-and-hiring-freeze-in-may\/","title":{"rendered":"Tech employees face another tough week of cross-stage layoffs"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">Unfortunately, there’s more where last week came from.
"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/06\/startup-tech-layoffs-in-may\/\"> Following last week’s slew of layoffs in tech<\/a>, this week had another dose of staff cuts across tech companies. Impact was felt across industries ranging from education to security, as well as stages from a post-Series A startup to a recently-SPAC’d business.<\/p>\nBelow, we’ve listed the latest companies that have laid off talent in response to the reset happening across startup land. Big shout out to"https:\/\/layoffs.fyi\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> Layoffs.fyi<\/a>, a tracker that aggregates tips, spreadsheets of impacted employees and other layoff details in one spot.<\/p>\nSection4<\/h2>\n"speakable-summary\">"https:\/\/www.section4.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Section4<\/a>, an up-skilling startup launched by prominent NYU professor\u00a0"https:\/\/twitter.com\/profgalloway\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Scott Galloway<\/a>, has laid off a quarter of staff, sources say. The layoffs, which occurred last week, affected employees across all levels of seniority and teams, but specifically targeted a majority of the product team. The startup first splashed onto the scene in 2019 with a goal to scale business school-quality courses in a more affordable, and entirely virtual, way.<\/p>\nCEO"https:\/\/twitter.com\/gregshove?lang=en\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">\u00a0Greg Shove<\/a>\u00a0confirmed layoff details to TechCrunch over e-mail and said that 32 people were impacted. The executive declined to disclose specifics on what impacted employees were offered, but said that the severance package was \u201cat market or better.\u201d Shove added that there is no hiring freeze and that the company will continue to employ folks in engineering and enterprise. Part of that hiring focus, he adds, is that the startup is moving faster in serving the enterprise than individual consumers, so hiring will reflect that.<\/p>\nLayoffs are a dramatic way to change strategies, but also signal that the company needs to play defense before it can entirely pivot. As we’ve been covering for months, consumer edtech has been flirting with selling to enterprises as to avoid revenue volatility"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/28\/employers-are-consumer-edtechs-next-beta-test\/\">(and land stickier contracts).<\/a><\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Yup4IQY9eE\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/12\/professor-scott-galloways-edtech-startup-section-4-lay-offs\/\">Scott Galloway\u2019s edtech startup, Section4, lays off a quarter of staff<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“Scott Galloway\u2019s edtech startup, Section4, lays off a quarter of staff” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/12\/professor-scott-galloways-edtech-startup-section-4-lay-offs\/embed\/#?secret=bsdhoxRpAG#?secret=Yup4IQY9eE\" data-secret=\"Yup4IQY9eE\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\nCarvana<\/h2>\nCarvana, the used-car retailer that went public in 2017,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/10\/carvana-to-cut-2500-staff-as-it-struggles-with-overcapacity\/\">laid off 2,500 staff\u00a0<\/a>as part of the company\u2019s \u201cpreviously announced plans to better align staffing and expense levels with sales volumes,\u201d it claims"https:\/\/www.sec.gov\/ix?doc=\/Archives\/edgar\/data\/0001690820\/000119312522145982\/d272103d8k.htm\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">in a filing. <\/a>Per the same filing, reports Alex Wilhelm, the company is offering those laid off four weeks of pay plus an additional week for every year they’ve been at the company. The company claims that the executive team is forgoing their salaries for the remainder of the year to contribute to severance pay.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n"https:\/\/www.cnbc.com\/2022\/05\/12\/heavily-shorted-online-used-car-seller-carvana-surges-35percent-is-halted-several-times.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The mobility meets e-commerce startup surged on Thursday,<\/a> after earlier hitting a two-year low. I guess that’s how the market responds to people losing jobs? A Short squeeze?<\/p>\nLatch<\/h2>\nLatch, an enterprise SaaS company that makes keyless-entry systems, has been struggling for the past few months — from experiencing a difficult SPAC debut to"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/04\/latch-cfo-out-after-spac\/\">parting ways with its CFO, Garth Mitchell. <\/a>Well, it looks like the business volatility has now trickled down to employees with the public company reportedly cutting 30 people, or 6% of its total staff, per an e-mail obtained by TechCrunch.<\/p>\nDataRobot<\/h2>\nIn 2019, DataRobot had just raised a"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/09\/17\/boston-based-datarobot-raises-206m-series-e-to-bring-ai-to-enterprise\/\">$206 million Series E round<\/a> from Sapphire Ventures, Tiger Global Management and a number of other firms. Then, just weeks after COVID-19 arrived in the U.S., the Boston-based machine learning company conducted layoffs due to “"https:\/\/www.bizjournals.com\/boston\/inno\/stories\/news\/2020\/03\/27\/datarobot-cuts-workforce-as-coronavirus-roils-the.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">uncertainty<\/a>.” Fast-forward to the present, DataRobot laid off another 7% of its workforce this week.\u00a0With about 1,000 employees, these layoffs are estimated to affect around 70 people. In an email to staff obtained by"https:\/\/www.theinformation.com\/briefings\/ai-startup-datarobot-lays-off-7-in-cost-cutting-move\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The Information<\/a>, CEO Dan Wright said that the layoffs were a response to changing market conditions after aggressive hiring last year ("https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/06\/startup-tech-layoffs-in-may\/?tpcc=tcplustwitter\">a trend<\/a> we saw across layoffs last week).<\/p>\n\u201cThat level of investment is no longer sustainable for our business, particularly in the context of broader changes in the market, with investors now taking a harder look at efficiency and spending,\u201d he said in the email.<\/p>\nMeta and Twitter freeze while Uber rethinks<\/h2>\nBut wait, there’s more… On the heels of iffy Q1 earnings reports, some big tech companies are in trouble.<\/p>\nLet’s start with Meta n\u00e9e Facebook. Mark Zuckerberg is all-in on building the metaverse, having just opened its first"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/25\/meta-store-facebook-store\/\">brick-and-mortar store<\/a>. He also just demoed what’s to come on the company’s next headset, dubbed “"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/12\/mark-zuckerberg-shows-off-metas-next-headset-kind-of\/\">Project Cambria<\/a>,” which will incorporate mixed reality into the headset. But in"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/27\/meta-facebook-q1-2022-earnings\/\">Q1 alone<\/a>, Meta\u2019s Reality Labs — its VR and AR team — operated at a loss of $2.96 billion, and last year, Reality Labs lost"https:\/\/www.cnbc.com\/2022\/02\/02\/meta-reality-labs-reports-10-billion-loss.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">over $10 billion<\/a>. Meanwhile, Facebook’s user growth has become relatively stagnant.<\/p>\nLast week, Insider"https:\/\/www.businessinsider.com\/leaked-facebook-memo-details-hiring-freeze-negative-business-impacts-2022-5\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">reported<\/a> that Facebook CFO David Wehner wrote in an internal memo that hiring will be paused across most engineering teams for the rest of the year, citing an “industry-wide downturn.” Then, this week, Reuters reported that Meta is preparing"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/technology\/exclusive-facebook-owner-meta-tells-hardware-staffers-prepare-cutbacks-2022-05-11\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">cutbacks<\/a> in Reality Labs, a bad omen for its… burgeoning metaverse business.\u00a0Some candidates for jobs at Meta have had their offers rescinded, per a"https:\/\/www.linkedin.com\/feed\/update\/urn:li:activity:6928376497523109888\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">viral LinkedIn post<\/a>.<\/p>\nTwitter employees are also facing a moment of uncertainty as they await"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/24\/elon-musk-twitter-offer-timeline\/\">Elon Musk’s impending takeover<\/a>. Yesterday, CEO Parag Agrawal — who is expected to be replaced after Musk’s acquisition clears — asked"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/12\/top-twitter-execs-including-heads-of-revenue-and-consumer-products-are-out-following-musk-deal\/\">two key executives<\/a> to leave. The company is also undergoing a hiring freeze, which isn’t uncommon following M&A deals.<\/p>\n\u201cEffective this week, we are pausing most hiring and backfills, except for business-critical roles. We are also pulling back on non-labor costs to ensure we are being responsible and efficient,\u201d a Twitter spokesperson told TechCrunch.<\/p>\nAnd then that brings us to Uber, which is"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/07\/uber-boosts-q1-profit-guidance-as-the-world-gets-moving-again\/\">valued lower<\/a> now than it was in mid-2019.<\/p>\n“It\u2019s clear that the market is experiencing a seismic shift and we need to react accordingly,” CEO Dara Khosrowshahi"https:\/\/www.cnbc.com\/2022\/05\/09\/uber-to-cut-down-on-costs-treat-hiring-as-a-privilege-ceo-email.html\">wrote<\/a>. He added, “We will treat hiring as a privilege and be deliberate about when and where we add headcount. We will be even more hardcore about costs across the board.”<\/p>\nIt’s not easy to navigate the pandemic as a company that requires drivers and passengers to sit together in a car. But, Khosrowshahi’s note highlighted investors’ interest in products like Uber Eats, which set their service apart from competitors like Lyft. Still, food delivery"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/14\/food-delivery-profits-remain-elusive\/\">isn’t the most profitable<\/a> business either.<\/p>\nUnfortunately, it’s usually the workers who get the short end of the stick in these situations, whether they’re tech staff or contracted gig workers.<\/p>\nKhosrowshahi ended his note with an attempt at optimism (?) in a turbulent time.<\/p>\n“GO GET IT!” he said.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"tkv5rWbXNj\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/tech-layoffs-dont-happen-to-companies-they-happen-to-people\/\">Tech layoffs don’t happen to companies, they happen to people<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“Tech layoffs don’t happen to companies, they happen to people” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/tech-layoffs-dont-happen-to-companies-they-happen-to-people\/embed\/#?secret=rSddQLDQ6Q#?secret=tkv5rWbXNj\" data-secret=\"tkv5rWbXNj\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"W0NqwykQzv\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/12\/top-twitter-execs-including-heads-of-revenue-and-consumer-products-are-out-following-musk-deal\/\">Top Twitter execs, including heads of revenue and consumer products, are out following Musk deal<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; \/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=4621"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=4621"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2317916,"date":"2022-05-12T14:55:23","date_gmt":"2022-05-12T21:55:23","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2317916"},"modified":"2022-05-12T15:09:21","modified_gmt":"2022-05-12T22:09:21","slug":"russia-ukraine-social-media-war-crimes-congress","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/12\/russia-ukraine-social-media-war-crimes-congress\/","title":{"rendered":"Congress asks Meta, TikTok, YouTube and Twitter to archive evidence of Russian war crimes"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">Four U.S. representatives"https:\/\/oversight.house.gov\/news\/press-releases\/oversight-and-foreign-affairs-committees-call-on-social-media-companies-to\">signed letters<\/a> to the CEOs of Meta, TikTok, YouTube and Twitter urging them to archive any content uploaded to their platforms that could be used as evidence of Russian war crimes.<\/p>\nAs TikTok booms in popularity and"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/27\/tiktok-reached-1-billion-monthly-active-users\/\">surpasses 1 billion users<\/a>, the rise of short-form video has offered unprecedented access to live footage from war zones — not to mention that Meta, YouTube and Twitter continue to capture our attention, too. These members of congress — Representatives Carolyn Maloney (D-NY), Gregory Meeks (D-NY), Stephen Lynch (D-MA) and William Keating (D-MA) — think that social media uploads can be instrumental in holding the perpetrators of human rights violations accountable.<\/p>\nGraphic wartime videos are often removed from social platforms, since they can violate terms of service that prohibit violent content. But according to a Human Rights Watch (HRW)"https:\/\/www.hrw.org\/report\/2020\/09\/10\/video-unavailable\/social-media-platforms-remove-evidence-war-crimes\">report<\/a>, which is cited in these letters to CEOs, it’s not clear what happens to these videos once they’re removed from the public-facing apps. Facebook, for example, says it keeps deleted data for at least 90 days, but Facebook told the HRW that it sometimes retains data for longer when requested by law enforcement.<\/p>\n“We are concerned that social media platforms [ \u2026 ] do not have adequate procedures in place to archive this content so that it can be made available to international organizations conducting investigations into allegations of war crimes and other atrocities,” the representatives’"https:\/\/oversight.house.gov\/news\/press-releases\/oversight-and-foreign-affairs-committees-call-on-social-media-companies-to\">statement<\/a> reads.<\/p>\nIn particular, the four representatives are calling on these platforms to preserve and archive potentially useful content for an extended period of time; coordinate with international human rights organizations to develop a legal, established way to share such content; increase transparency around AI-based content moderation systems and how they interface with war content; and, creating a way for users to flag content that they think might contain evidence of war crimes.<\/p>\n“Photos, videos and other content posted on social media have increasingly supported accountability processes, including judicial proceedings, for serious international crimes, both at the national and international level,” the HRW report"https:\/\/www.hrw.org\/report\/2020\/09\/10\/video-unavailable\/social-media-platforms-remove-evidence-war-crimes\">explains<\/a>. The HRW states that there have been at least 10 cases in Germany, Finland, the Netherlands and Sweden where people involved in war crimes in Iraq and Syria have been persecuted using evidence from social media posts.<\/p>\nThough this evidence can aid international legal systems, these bodies will also have to be careful not to fall prey to misinformation, which may be used to facilitate a wrongful conviction. Since Russia’s invasion of Ukraine in February, there have been many instances of fake videos going viral on social media, like"https:\/\/www.nytimes.com\/2022\/03\/05\/technology\/tiktok-ukraine-misinformation.html\">video game footage<\/a> that’s presented as though it were filmed on the ground in Ukraine.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nTechCrunch has reached out to Meta, TikTok, YouTube and Twitter for comment. media","slug":"social-media","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/49818"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=49818"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=49818"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=49818"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=49818"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2316279,"date":"2022-05-11T11:53:21","date_gmt":"2022-05-11T18:53:21","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2316279"},"modified":"2022-05-11T17:35:47","modified_gmt":"2022-05-12T00:35:47","slug":"fanhouse-creator-monetization-rosie-nguyen","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/11\/fanhouse-creator-monetization-rosie-nguyen\/","title":{"rendered":"Fanhouse was built by creators, for creators (and they mean it)"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">Rosie Nguyen isn’t your typical startup founder. Her"https:\/\/www.instagram.com\/jasminericegirl\/?hl=en\">Instagram<\/a> grid perfectly depicts the two sides of who she is: In one post, she\u2019s"https:\/\/www.instagram.com\/p\/CZQRCWgJbGO\/\">live on CNBC<\/a> speaking out against Apple\u2019s developer fees. In the next, she poses on a wood floor with the caption, \u201cday 89 without sex: sitting on the floor so I can feel hard wood under me.\u201d And then in the post after that, she\u2019s sharing her front page appearance in the Philadelphia Inquirer.<\/p>\nNguyen is the CMO of"http:\/\/fanhouse.app\">Fanhouse<\/a>, a creator monetization platform that rivals Patreon and OnlyFans, but at the same time that she’s building Fanhouse, she’s also building her career as a content creator. Online, Nguyen is known as"https:\/\/jasminericegirl.com\/\">jasminericegirl<\/a>, whether she’s streaming games like Valorant on Twitch or posting raunchy jokes to her 157,000 Twitter followers.<\/p>\n\u201cI am a creator at heart and I always will be, and just because I\u2019m also a founder now doesn\u2019t mean I\u2019m not a creator,\u201d Nguyen said. She sees these two sides of her persona as complementary, rather than at odds with one another, or — god forbid — unprofessional. \u201cIt\u2019s a positive thing that really goes hand in hand, and I think a good investor will see that.\u201d<\/p>\nAs it turns out, Nguyen was right. Fanhouse just secured a $20 million Series A round from Andreessen Horowitz, and the platform is about to surpass $10 million in creator payouts in less than two years. Its creators include The Chainsmokers (who are also"https:\/\/musically.com\/2021\/05\/28\/chainsmokers-vc-firm-invests-in-fan-funding-startup-fanhouse\/\">pre-seed investors<\/a>),"https:\/\/fanhouse.app\/andreabotez\/fanwall\">Andrea Botez<\/a>,"https:\/\/fanhouse.app\/yoshi_sudarso\/fanwall\">Yoshi Sudarso<\/a> and more.<\/p>\nIt\u2019s not unheard of for a YouTube star or TikTok sensation to be the face of a creator economy startup, but usually when this happens, it\u2019s with extremely established, high-earning names looking for new business opportunities, like MrBeast with"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/20\/creative-juice-investment-creators-youtube\/\">Creative Juice<\/a>, or David Dobrik with"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/21\/spark-capital-decides-to-sever-all-ties-with-david-dobriks-dispo-app-weeks-after-leading-investment\/\">Dispo<\/a>. As a young, emerging creator, Nguyen understands what the “creator middle class” — people who make some money on social media, but aren’t rolling in it — needs right now to grow their businesses.<\/p>\n\u201cI met Khoi [Le], my co-founder, on Twitter, and we became best friends,\u201d Nguyen told TechCrunch. \u201cI was telling him all these things like, OnlyFans sucks, I hate it, I want to get off of it but I need the money \u2026 Or like, Twitch takes 50% of subscriptions, it\u2019s so exhausting.\u201d<\/p>\nA Stanford graduate with an entrepreneurial background, Le told Nguyen that together, they could build her dream monetization platform, so they started experimenting with ideas that would later turn into Fanhouse. The founding trio is rounded out by CTO Amy Shen, who brings engineering experience from Robinhood and Google.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n"embed breakout\">\n"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n"en\" dir=\"ltr\">At 10, I was applying for EBT with my family because we didn't have food. At 13, I was sleeping in an office closet because we didn't have a home. At 19, I was working 3 jobs in college to pay our bills.<\/p>\nI'm 24 now, and I'm crying to be selected as a Forbes 30 Under 30 member.
"https:\/\/t.co\/Amxc7TnlZ1\">pic.twitter.com\/Amxc7TnlZ1<\/a><\/p>\n— jasminericegirl \ud83c\udf5a (@jasminericegirl)"https:\/\/twitter.com\/jasminericegirl\/status\/1466500893013159938?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">December 2, 2021<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n\u201cI was one of those people that never really knew if I had a dream job,\u201d Nguyen said. Growing up in a low-income household, her goal was simply to make enough money to pull her family out of poverty. When she graduated from the University of Pennsylvania\u2019s Wharton School, she took a job in investment banking for the salary alone. But soon, she found herself staying up late into the night to work on the idea for Fanhouse.<\/p>\n\u201cI realized I do have a dream job, and this is it,\u201d she said. \u201cI wouldn\u2019t say my passion is entrepreneurship, but my passion is helping content creators.\u201d<\/p>\nUnlike OnlyFans, Fanhouse doesn\u2019t allow NSFW content \u2014 too many hoops to jump through with credit card companies and fundraising. Nguyen isn’t opposed to the idea, but she thinks that there needs to be “a more societal and legal shift” before that could feasibly work for Fanhouse. OnlyFans faced its own debacle last year when it"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/25\/onlyfans-suspends-decision-to-ban-explicit-content\/\">nearly banned<\/a> NSFW content due to changing guidelines of credit card companies.<\/p>\nFans can pay a monthly fee to access exclusive content, which includes text, photo, video and audio uploads. Fanhouse also just implemented an integration with Spotify, so for example, if you’re one of the top listeners of The Chainsmokers, you can subscribe to them on Fanhouse for free.<\/p>\nBut what sets the platform apart is its commitment to protecting creators. This is, of course, related to Nguyen\u2019s own experiences in the public eye.<\/p>\n\u201cOn Twitter, I\u2019ll receive unsolicited dick pics, report them and never get a reply from Twitter,\u201d Nguyen said. She also recalls receiving threats from subscribers on OnlyFans. \u201cAll these problems that I experience on platforms, I set out to change.\u201d<\/p>\nAs Nguyen"https:\/\/twitter.com\/fanhouse\/status\/1521186154946523136\">tweeted<\/a> from the Fanhouse account last week: \u201cjust a reminder that when someone leaks private content from fanhouse, not only will our support team trace down who leaked it to fine and deactivate them, but they’ll also DMCA the site. we’ve taken down entire subreddits and discord servers before. do not mess with our creators.\u201d<\/p>\nNguyen says that Fanhouse is able to take down leaks and find out who leaked exclusive content because every creator upload is watermarked. Each fan has their own personal watermark, so if they are leaking content, Fanhouse can trace the leak back to their account.<\/p>\nEvery account on Fanhouse also has to be connected to a phone number, and if a user gets banned once, then they can\u2019t make another account with that phone number again.<\/p>\nWhen it comes to payments, Fanhouse takes 10% of creator earnings, which is small compared to OnlyFans\u2019 20% or Twitch’s 50-50 split. But despite being a new app with about 25 team members, Fanhouse has already stood up to Apple over its 30% cut of in-app purchases.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Fanhouse is a start-up I founded to empower creators, and we pay our creators 90% of transactions.
\/>Apple is kicking us off the app store unless we give them 30% of all transactions.
\/>Apple is a trillion-dollar company, and they get there by exploiting the labor of others. (1\/)<\/p>\n— jasminericegirl \ud83c\udf5a (@jasminericegirl)"https:\/\/twitter.com\/jasminericegirl\/status\/1486414212381360131?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">January 26, 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\nApple’s 30% cut is hugely controversial — Fortnite creator Epic Games"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/10\/apple-prohibited-from-blocking-outside-payment-in-epic-ruling\/\">took the tech giant to court<\/a> over it.<\/p>\n“If a subscription was $10, and someone paid an app $10, the creator just gets $6 now,” Nguyen explained.<\/p>\nSo, Fanhouse developed “coins,” an in-app currency that fans can buy on the web, then pay to creators on the app without fees, since the coins are already loaded onto their account. If a fan wants to buy coins in the app, they’ll be charged an extra 50% to account for Apple’s cut, incentivizing them to just make the purchase on the web. Other platforms like Twitch try to do this by selling in-app currency like “bits,” which can be purchased online and doled out on the app.<\/p>\n“It’s not the easiest way to get creators paid; now there’s just an extra step, but we’d rather take that extra step, because the other alternative is that creator’s earnings are directly taken away from them,” she said.<\/p>\nFounding a startup is always a risk, and for Nguyen, the risk is personal — she still wants to fulfill her goal of supporting her family, and that surely would have been easier if she stayed in investment banking. But so far, her decision feels like it was worth it.<\/p>\n“[Growing up], we were always scraping by,” she remembers. “But I’d rather be doing Fanhouse and live like that than do banking and be more stable.”<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"uKeRIkn80i\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/30\/not-every-creator-economy-startup-is-built-for-creators\/\">Not every creator economy startup is built for creators<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“Not every creator economy startup is built for creators” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/30\/not-every-creator-economy-startup-is-built-for-creators\/embed\/#?secret=j9wxTcxd4j#?secret=uKeRIkn80i\" data-secret=\"uKeRIkn80i\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Km5bqJJCPH\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/20\/linktree-creator-economy-report-research\/\">Only 12% of full-time creators make over $50K a year, says Linktree<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“Only 12% of full-time creators make over $50K a year, says Linktree” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/20\/linktree-creator-economy-report-research\/embed\/#?secret=AdrLziqRgz#?secret=Km5bqJJCPH\" data-secret=\"Km5bqJJCPH\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"Rosie Nguyen isn’t your typical startup founder.
