New York Times edits Wordle answer list after Roe v. Wade leak"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">Perhaps you played the Wordle this morning and encountered a pretty ordinary five-letter word. But if you haven’t refreshed your page over the last week, you could’ve encountered the solution “FETUS,” which The New York Times decided was a bit too closely linked to current events — last week, Politico"https:\/\/www.politico.com\/news\/2022\/05\/02\/supreme-court-abortion-draft-opinion-00029473\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">leaked<\/a> a Supreme Court opinion draft that is poised to"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/05\/roe-wade-privacy-period-tracking\/\">overturn Roe v. Wade<\/a>, reversing the constitutional right to an abortion.<\/p>\nThe New York Times changed today’s solution to a word that’s less politically charged, though the original solution might still appear for users who haven’t reloaded the game.<\/p>\n“Some users may see an outdated answer that seems closely connected to a major recent news event. This is entirely unintentional and a coincidence,” wrote New York Times Games editorial director Everdeen Mason in a"https:\/\/www.nytimes.com\/2022\/05\/09\/crosswords\/a-note-about-todays-wordle-game.html?smid=tw-nytimes&smtyp=cur\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">statement<\/a>, published right as today’s Wordle hit the web.<\/p>\nAs Mason explains, Wordle’s answers are predetermined in its code, pulling from an answer pool of five-letter words that founder Josh Wardle concocted over a year ago. Not all five-letter words appear in the list — he intentionally removed the most obscure five-letter words, since he wanted the game to be solvable more often than not (you also probably won’t encounter a four-letter noun with an added “S” at the end to make it plural).<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Some of you may have a different Wordle answer than the official answer. Please refresh your browser to receive the correct answer word. For more information, please read our editor\u2019s note.
"https:\/\/t.co\/3dY5nRu7yu\">https:\/\/t.co\/3dY5nRu7yu<\/a><\/p>\n— The New York Times (@nytimes)"https:\/\/twitter.com\/nytimes\/status\/1523514223317315584?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">May 9, 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n"css-at9mc1 evys1bk0\">“When we"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/31\/popular-puzzle-game-wordle-is-being-purchased-by-the-new-york-times\/\">acquired Wordle<\/a> in January, it had been built for a relatively small group of users,” Mason said. “We\u2019re now busy revamping Wordle\u2019s technology so that everyone always receives the same word.”<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nSince Wordle joined New York Times Games, there have been a few instances where there are"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/why-wordle-game-284-had-two-answers-and-how-to-fix\/\"> two possible solutions<\/a> to a Wordle. Most recently, this happened at the end of March, when users could have encountered either “STOVE” or “HARRY” as the answer.<\/p>\nThis happened because The New York Times removed some of the more obscure words left in the Wordle solution bank, such as “HARRY,” which is not the name of a boy wizard, but an outdated verb meaning “to persistently harass.” But when Wordle migrated from Wardle’s"http:\/\/powerlanguage.co.uk\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">personal website<\/a> to The New York Times, some users’ games were still pulling data from the original Wordle, not the slightly tweaked New York Times version.<\/p>\nThe New York Times says that “tens of millions” of people are playing Wordle each day. Its “"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/31\/popular-puzzle-game-wordle-is-being-purchased-by-the-new-york-times\/\">low seven figures<\/a>” acquisition of the delightfully simple game seems to be paying off, as the company said it had its"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/04\/wordle-new-york-times-user-growth\/\">best quarter ever<\/a> for user growth in its subscription-based Games section.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"MNzAM7JgAG\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/04\/wordle-new-york-times-user-growth\/\">Wordle brought ‘tens of millions’ of new users to the New York Times<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; New York wide web","slug":"world-wide-web","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/2648"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=2648"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=2648"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=2648"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=2648"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2313868,"date":"2022-05-06T12:17:10","date_gmt":"2022-05-06T19:17:10","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2313868"},"modified":"2022-05-06T16:05:53","modified_gmt":"2022-05-06T23:05:53","slug":"startup-tech-layoffs-in-may","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/06\/startup-tech-layoffs-in-may\/","title":{"rendered":"Post-pandemic reset leads to wave of layoffs in tech"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">OK, maybe it is"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/12\/its-not-a-startup-reckoning-its-a-recorrection\/\">a reckoning<\/a>.<\/p>\nOver the past week, we\u2019ve witnessed an alarming amount of layoffs across the startup ecosystem, from buzzy, big names like Cameo, On Deck and Robinhood, to B2B platforms like Workrise and Thrasio. The common thread between most of these layoffs, according to founders, is that there’s been a shift in the market and a serious pivot in business is required. A pivot, that is, that hurts the employees that built your product up after high demand.<\/p>\nA pullback has been in the cards for months. It first impacted public tech companies and then slowly trickled down to late-stage deals and even their well funded early-stage counterparts. In February,"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/10\/virtual-events-platform-hopin-cuts-12-of-staff-citing-goal-of-sustainable-growth\/\">Hopin cut 12% of staff, citing a goal of more sustainable growth<\/a>, while April included"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/05\/workrise-cuts-staff-verticals-after-being-valued-at-2-9b-last-year\/\">Workrise cutting staff and verticals despite a $2.9 billion valuation.<\/a><\/p>\nNow feels like an inflection point, in which tech unicorns are realizing that they may have overpromised a growth trajectory, over-hired or overestimated their ability to raise that next round. They aren’t alluding to the market changing, they’re blaming it. The irony here is tough: The same workforces that helped companies meet a boom in pandemic demand are the same workforces on the chopping block when trends change.<\/p>\nBelow, we’ve listed which companies announced layoffs this week to underscore the unfortunate, albeit growing, trend.<\/p>\nSaaS company Mural cuts dozens of staff<\/h3>\nSoftware-as-a-service startups often get the reputation of being predictable, and therefore perfect for the risk-adverse investor.
"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/21\/why-saas-is-bucking-the-venture-slowdown\/\"> While stable business models have protected SaaS companies<\/a> from the venture slowdown for quite some time, TechCrunch is hearing that digital collaboration startup platform Mural just cut dozens of staff. Per sources and LinkedIn posts from laid-off employees, the layoffs came after a corporate restructuring at the SaaS company. Sales and customer success folks were impacted. Also notably, the reduction comes less than a year after"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/20\/mural-raises-50m-series-c-after-tripling-its-arr-in-the-last-year\/\">Mural raised a $50 million Series C after tripling its ARR.<\/a><\/p>\n"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/04\/cameo-layoff-unicorn\/\">Cameo conducts layoffs a year after hitting unicorn status <\/a><\/h3>\nGetting laid off sucks. Getting laid off sucks even more when your Bored Ape-owning CEO tweets that he made the \u201cpainful decision to let go of 87 beloved members of the Cameo Fameo.\u201d Damn, at least spare them from the corporate nicknaming in your farewell tweet.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nThese layoffs included teams across all organizations, including several C-suite members. In a statement to TechCrunch, CEO Steven Galanis said that Cameo\u2019s headcount \u201cexploded\u201d from 100 to 400 during pandemic lockdowns, but that now the company \u201cright-sized the business to best reflect the new realities.\u201d<\/p>\nEmployees who spoke to TechCrunch on the condition of anonymity said that they will receive severance packages that include eight weeks of base salary.<\/p>\n"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/26\/robinhood-to-lay-off-9-of-full-time-employees\/\">Robinhood to lay off 9% of full-time employees<\/a><\/h3>\nThe gamified consumer investing app Robinhood cut about 300 employees at the end of April, and like Cameo, the company cited an inability to keep up with early-pandemic acceleration. CEO Vlad Tenev wrote in a"https:\/\/blog.robinhood.com\/news\/2022\/4\/26\/a-message-from-our-ceo-and-co-founder-vlad-tenev\">blog post<\/a> that the company\u2019s headcount grew from 700 to nearly 3,800 from 2019 to 2021.<\/p>\n\u201cAfter carefully considering all these factors, we determined that making these reductions to Robinhood\u2019s staff is the right decision to improve efficiency, increase our velocity, and ensure that we are responsive to the changing needs of our customers,\u201d he added.<\/p>\nDays later, Robinhood announced its Q1 2022 earnings, which"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/29\/robinhoods-sinking-value-is-proof-that-free-can-often-be-very-costly\/\">fell far below<\/a> expectations.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"XBZ9VMgjO0\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/04\/robinhood-rolls-out-stock-lending-margin-diversify-revenue\/\">Robinhood to let users lend out their shares in its attempt to diversify revenue<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“Robinhood to let users lend out their shares in its attempt to diversify revenue” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/04\/robinhood-rolls-out-stock-lending-margin-diversify-revenue\/embed\/#?secret=G3SG1wQCyp#?secret=XBZ9VMgjO0\" data-secret=\"XBZ9VMgjO0\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/05\/on-deck-lay-off-accelerator\/\">On Deck cuts 25% of staff, scales back accelerator<\/a><\/h3>\nOn Deck, a tech company that connects founders, laid off about 72 people this week, which amounts to about 25% of staff.<\/p>\nIn an email obtained by TechCrunch, co-founders Erik Torenberg and David Booth explained to staff that the market has \u201cshifted dramatically\u201d since 2021, when On Deck launched its ODX accelerator program. This program gives early-stage startups $125,000 in exchange for 7% of the company, backing over 150 companies to date, bringing the total investment to almost $19 million. But sources close to the company said that ODX will likely be scaled back or even shut down.<\/p>\nTechCrunch\u2019s sources also alleged that the company was attempting to raise a fund between $100 and $150 million, but in reality, they landed a fund closer to $40 million, leaving them with just nine months of runway. Hence, layoffs, mostly in operations and investing roles.<\/p>\nOn Deck\u2019s severance packages include eight weeks of paid base salary and 12 weeks of healthcare.<\/p>\n"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/02\/amazon-aggregator-thrasio-begins-layoffs-names-new-ceo\/\">Amazon aggregator Thrasio begins layoffs, names new CEO<\/a><\/h3>\nThrasio\u2019s business model is to buy up and consolidate third-party Amazon sellers, but apparently, that strategy is rife with ups and downs. After being rumored to go public, Thrasio raised $1 billion in funding last year, valuing the company at $10 billion.<\/p>\nIn a memo to employees, the company implied it was growing too big, too quickly.<\/p>\n\u201cNow, as we assess our strategy for the road ahead, we need to take the time to properly absorb and grow the businesses we have acquired, make sure we have rigorous processes and controls, and then look to re-scale our team in the optimal areas for growth,\u201d the note said.<\/p>\nThrasio\u2019s internal shake-up doesn\u2019t end with layoffs, though — the aggregator is also installing Greg Greeley as its new CEO. Greeley formerly was president of Airbnb and a longtime Amazon executive.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"xlysaNR5NW\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/19\/how-many-unicorns-are-just-pinatas-filled-with-expired-candy\/\">How many unicorns are just pi\u00f1atas filled with expired candy?<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“How many unicorns are just pi\u00f1atas filled with expired candy?” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/19\/how-many-unicorns-are-just-pinatas-filled-with-expired-candy\/embed\/#?secret=5CebVW0vhn#?secret=xlysaNR5NW\" data-secret=\"xlysaNR5NW\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/28\/netflix-layoffs-tudum-editorial\/\">Netflix layoffs hit Tudum, its editorial arm, just five months after launch<\/a><\/h3>\nLast year on \u201cjournalism Twitter,\u201d it seemed like every day, a great culture reporter was leaving sites like BuzzFeed and Vice to work for Tudum, a burgeoning editorial project at Netflix. It makes sense why. One staffer told BuzzFeed that they were making"https:\/\/www.buzzfeednews.com\/article\/davidmack\/netflix-tudum-layoffs-cruel-to-writers\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">three times as much money<\/a> at Netflix than at their previous job.<\/p>\nMedia workers are no stranger to layoffs, and perhaps a job at a massive tech company seemed more stable than working somewhere that recently laid off employees in a Zoom meeting with the password"https:\/\/www.nytimes.com\/2021\/03\/09\/business\/media\/huffpost-layoffs-buzzfeed.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">\u201cspr!ngisH3r3<\/a>.\u201d But sometimes, the tech industry can be equally as cruel.<\/p>\nThe project was championed by chief marketing officer Bozoma Saint John, who left Netflix last month after less than two years. That departure left Tudum on shaky footing. Plus, Netflix reported that in the"https:\/\/ir.netflix.net\/investor-news-and-events\/investor-events\/event-details\/2022\/Netflix-First-Quarter-2022-Earnings-Interview\/default.aspx\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">first quarter<\/a> of 2022, it lost 200,000 subscribers \u2014 its first subscriber loss in more than a decade. These losses are expected to continue, as Netflix forecasts a global paid subscriber loss of 2 million for the second quarter.<\/p>\nThe layoffs reportedly affected 25 people total across Netflix\u2019s marketing department. According to a tweet from a laid-off writer, the staff was only offered two weeks of severance pay.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"OkMa0FlfxW\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/20\/netflix-subscriber-decline-suggests-the-streamer-is-in-need-of-better-content\/\">Is it cake? No, it’s Netflix’s crumbling subscriber numbers<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“Is it cake? No, it’s Netflix’s crumbling subscriber numbers” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/20\/netflix-subscriber-decline-suggests-the-streamer-is-in-need-of-better-content\/embed\/#?secret=W6A0iZVG08#?secret=OkMa0FlfxW\" data-secret=\"OkMa0FlfxW\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/05\/fintech-mainstreet-layoffs\/\">Fintech MainStreet cuts about 30% of staff, citing \u2018incredibly rough market\u2019<\/a><\/h3>\n"https:\/\/www.mainstreet.com\/\">MainStreet<\/a>, a startup that helps other startups uncover tax credits that was\u00a0"https:\/\/www.theinformation.com\/articles\/mainstreet-which-finds-tax-credits-for-startups-valued-at-500-million\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">valued at $500 million<\/a>\u00a0last year, has laid off about 30% of its staff, according to a\u00a0"https:\/\/twitter.com\/dougludlow\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">tweet<\/a> from CEO Doug Ludlow. The chief executive said that “today’s incredibly rough market” is going to get worse and could remain for months, if not years. Like many fintechs, MainStreet is a startup that depend on other startups growing — making it especially vulnerable to any sort of pull back.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"oJoZOEYU6b\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/10\/fintech-roundup-fast-and-better-com-show-us-that-humility-is-an-underrated-ceo-trait\/\">Fintech Roundup: How going Fast and furious can ruin your startup<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“Fintech Roundup: How going Fast and furious can ruin your startup” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/10\/fintech-roundup-fast-and-better-com-show-us-that-humility-is-an-underrated-ceo-trait\/embed\/#?secret=D3rWOH54hW#?secret=oJoZOEYU6b\" data-secret=\"oJoZOEYU6b\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\nIf you have been impacted by a startup layoff, reach out to Natasha Mascarenhas or Amanda Silberling via e-mail or Twitter DM:"https:\/\/twitter.com\/nmasc_\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">@nmasc_<\/a> or"https:\/\/twitter.com\/asilbwrites\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">@asilbwrites<\/a>.<\/em><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"OK, maybe it is a reckoning. Over the past week, we\u2019ve witnessed an alarming amount of layoffs across the startup ecosystem, from buzzy, big names like Cameo, On Deck and Robinhood, to B2B platforms like Workrise and Thrasio. The common thread between most of these layoffs, according to founders, is that there’s been a shift companies?tags=4621"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=4621"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=4621"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":318,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/tech\/","name":"Tech","slug":"tech","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/318"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=318"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=318"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=318"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=318"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576788868,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/thrasio\/","name":"thrasio","slug":"thrasio","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576788868"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576788868"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576788868"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576788868"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576788868"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2312916,"date":"2022-05-05T14:21:33","date_gmt":"2022-05-05T21:21:33","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2312916"},"modified":"2022-05-05T14:50:45","modified_gmt":"2022-05-05T21:50:45","slug":"amazon-labor-senate-christian-smalls-bernie-sanders","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/05\/amazon-labor-senate-christian-smalls-bernie-sanders\/","title":{"rendered":"Amazon Labor Union president tells Senate that workers’ rights aren’t a ‘Democrat or Republican’ issue"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">Back in February, Amazon tried to"http:\/\/reuters.com\/business\/amazon-labor-organizer-smalls-arrested-faces-trespass-charge-after-dropping-off-2022-02-24\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">arrest<\/a> labor organizer Christian Smalls for bringing food to warehouse employees during a union drive. One unfathomably monumental labor victory later, and today, the New Yorker is speaking before the Senate and visiting President Joe Biden at the White House.<\/p>\nSmalls, the Amazon Labor Union president who led the JFK8 warehouse’s"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/01\/staten-island-amazon-workers-vote-to-unionize\/\">historic union win<\/a>, testified today in a"https:\/\/www.budget.senate.gov\/hearings\/should-taxpayer-dollars-go-to-companies-that-violate-labor-laws\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">hearing<\/a> for the Senate Committee on the Budget. Chaired by Senator Bernie Sanders (I-VT), the hearing posed the question of whether tax dollars should support companies that violate labor laws. Representatives from other groups like Good Jobs First, the Teamsters and the Heritage Foundation joined the hearing as well.<\/p>\n“The types of things Amazon is doing… Breaking the law, intimidation… These are real things that traumatize workers in this country,” Smalls said in his opening statement. “We want to feel that we have protections. We want to feel that the government is allowing us to use our constitutional rights to organize.”<\/p>\nAcross the country, Amazon workers have"https:\/\/www.nytimes.com\/2021\/03\/16\/technology\/amazon-unions-virginia.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">accused the company<\/a>\u00a0of trying to quash labor organizing. Last year, Amazonians United co-founder Jonathan Bailey\u00a0"https:\/\/www.nbcnews.com\/business\/business-news\/fired-interrogated-disciplined-amazon-warehouse-organizers-allege-year-retaliation-n1262367\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">filed a complaint<\/a>\u00a0with the National Labor Relations Board (NLRB), stating that the company violated labor laws by retaliating against him for organizing. He said he was detained and interrogated by a manager for 90 minutes after organizing a walkout. The NLRB found merit to these allegations and filed a federal complaint against Amazon. The company settled, and as part of the settlement agreement, was required to remind employees via emails and on physical bulletin boards that they have the right to organize.<\/p>\nBailey\u2019s complaint to the NLRB was one of 37 against Amazon between February 2020 and March 2021, according to"https:\/\/www.nbcnews.com\/business\/business-news\/fired-interrogated-disciplined-amazon-warehouse-organizers-allege-year-retaliation-n1262367\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">NBC News<\/a>. But just months after this settlement, Amazon was found to have\u00a0"https:\/\/www.vice.com\/en\/article\/bvz3kv\/amazon-unlawfully-confiscated-union-literature-nlrb-finds\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">unlawfully prevented<\/a> a Staten Island employee from distributing pro-union literature in the break room. Amazon filings with the Department of Labor revealed that the company spent"https:\/\/www.engadget.com\/amazon-spent-43-million-on-anti-union-consultants-in-2021-alone-082051777.html?guccounter=1&guce_referrer=aHR0cHM6Ly93d3cuZ29vZ2xlLmNvbS8&guce_referrer_sig=AQAAAIhb5L01i9YY-C_vmIb42wZkXtBfjRBelkrz5X_M7J-UV1DsCzjooxt1XKE8ZjDsUdmyRu4iLgAgwtTNfxTeW04OX0eFTZSLqgxp9UhjMtE0Vu6p0Jd4cf3Z_tc75tNa_UZ1Pmze0nffGuhbiAe8BhAMz3RHYCKGZmCVZgUSzH7Q\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">$4.3 million<\/a> on anti-union consultants last year alone.<\/p>\nSenator Lindsey Graham (R-SC) defended Amazon, accusing Senator Sanders of unfairly targeting the company.<\/p>\n“You’re singling out a single company because of your political agenda to socialize this country,” Senator Graham said. “Every time I turn around, you’re having a hearing about [how] anybody who makes money is bad.”<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nGraham outlined that the NLRB has a process in place for workers to file complaints if they feel they are being treated unfairly, saying that he disagreed with a Senate hearing taking place at all.<\/p>\n“You can have oversight hearings all you like, but you’ve determined Amazon is a piece of crap company. That’s your political bias,” Graham told Sanders. “[Amazon is] subject to laws in the United States, they shouldn’t be subjected to this.”<\/p>\n"attachment_2312945\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2312945\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2312945\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/GettyImages-1240211375.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"Amazon Labor Union founder Christian Smalls speaks at a rally on Staten Island in April 2022.\" width=\"680\" height=\"453\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/GettyImages-1240211375.jpg 3000w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/GettyImages-1240211375.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/GettyImages-1240211375.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/GettyImages-1240211375.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/GettyImages-1240211375.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/GettyImages-1240211375.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/GettyImages-1240211375.jpg?resize=2048,1365 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/GettyImages-1240211375.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2312945\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Christian Smalls, founder of the Amazon Labor Union (ALU), speaks during an ALU rally in the Staten Island borough of New York, U.S., on Sunday, April 24, 2022. Senator Bernie Sanders visited Staten Island to meet with workers who this month successfully organized the first union in the country at an Amazon facility and workers at a separate facility who will be voting next week on whether to join a union. Photographer: Victor J. Blue\/Bloomberg via Getty Images<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nIn response, Smalls directed his opening statement to Senator Graham.<\/p>\n“I think that it’s in your best interest to realize that it’s not a left or right thing. It’s not a Democrat or Republican thing. It’s a workers’ issue,” Small told the senator. “We are the ones that are suffering in the corporations that you’re talking about, […] in the warehouses that you’re talking about. So that’s the reason why I think I was invited today to speak on that behalf, and you should listen, because we do represent your constituents as well.”<\/p>\nHe continued, “The people are the ones that make these corporations go, it’s not the other way around.”<\/p>\nAt Senator Sanders’ urging, Smalls explained the working conditions of the now-unionizing fulfillment center where he used to work. He said that workers commuted from all boroughs of New York, as well as parts of New Jersey, which meant that they would commute for about two and a half hours each way, work a 10- to 12-hour shift, and receive minimal break time. He testified that hundreds of union busters came in from across the country, as well as from overseas. These representatives would host “captive audience” anti-union meetings every 20 minutes with groups of 50 to 60 workers. Smalls said that these captive audience presentations happened four times per week.<\/p>\n“Imagine being a new hire at Amazon. Your second day, you don’t even know your job assignment, and the first thing they do is march you into an anti-union propaganda class,” Smalls said. He added that the facility was plastered with anti-union signs, telling workers to vote no to unionization and emphasizing that unions require a dues expense on the workers’ part.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Just met the President lol he said I got him in trouble \ud83d\ude08 gooooooooooood"https:\/\/twitter.com\/amazonlabor?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@amazonlabor<\/a> \u270a\ud83c\udffd<\/p>\n— Christian Smalls (@Shut_downAmazon)"https:\/\/twitter.com\/Shut_downAmazon\/status\/1522296192406802437?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">May 5, 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\nThe hearing also addressed the Protecting the Right to Organize (PRO) Act, which recently passed in the House. Currently, in 27 “"https:\/\/www.ncsl.org\/research\/labor-and-employment\/right-to-work-laws-and-bills.aspx\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">right-to-work<\/a>” states, employees cannot be forced to join a union or pay dues, but if the PRO Act passed, it would"https:\/\/www.hrw.org\/news\/2021\/04\/29\/why-us-pro-act-matters-right-unionize-questions-and-answers\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">override<\/a> “right-to-work” laws. Union organizers believe, though, that “right-to-work” laws exist to"https:\/\/aflcio.org\/issues\/right-work\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">discourage unionization<\/a>, since it’s already federally illegal to force someone to join a union. If the PRO Act passes in the Senate (which isn’t expected, since Democrats don’t have enough seats to overcome the filibuster), it would be one of the"https:\/\/www.npr.org\/2021\/03\/09\/975259434\/house-democrats-pass-bill-that-would-protect-worker-organizing-efforts\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">biggest reforms<\/a> of labor legislation since the National Labor Relations Act of 1935, which protects the rights of employees to organize.<\/p>\nAfter the hearing, Smalls and a number of other labor organizers"https:\/\/finance.yahoo.com\/news\/amazon-com-union-organizer-meets-193827242.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">visited<\/a> President Biden at the White House.<\/p>\n“Just met the President lol he said I got him in trouble,” Smalls tweeted, likely referring to the backlash Biden experienced after"https:\/\/www.nytimes.com\/2022\/04\/06\/us\/politics\/biden-amazon-workers-labor-unions.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">expressing support<\/a> for the Amazon union — “gooooooooooood.”<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"abKyRgUIng\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/01\/staten-island-amazon-workers-vote-to-unionize\/\">Staten Island Amazon workers vote to unionize<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; Labor Relations Board","slug":"national-labor-relations-board","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576870670"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576870670"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576870670"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576870670"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576870670"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2312580,"date":"2022-05-05T09:01:38","date_gmt":"2022-05-05T16:01:38","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2312580"},"modified":"2022-05-05T11:54:52","modified_gmt":"2022-05-05T18:54:52","slug":"copper-books-app-authors","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/05\/copper-books-app-authors\/","title":{"rendered":"Copper is building ‘the Instagram for book lovers’"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">Any book lover knows the feeling: The incredible novel you’re reading ends with"https:\/\/www.penguinrandomhouse.com\/books\/609362\/the-last-graduate-by-naomi-novik\/\">a vicious cliffhanger<\/a>, and all you want to do is gab with other fans about what might happen next, but none of your friends have read the book. You might find fan discussions on Reddit, Tumblr or Discord, but it can be a bit of a crapshoot.<\/p>\nThe founder and CEO of"https:\/\/copperbooks.com\/\">Copper<\/a>, Allison Trowbridge wanted to build a social network that revolves around books, connecting authors and fans through in-app discussions and live events. As"https:\/\/bookshop.org\/books\/twenty-two-letters-to-a-young-woman-searching-for-meaning\/9780718078164\">an author herself<\/a>, she also wanted to help writers find new income streams, whether that’s through ticketed virtual events, or just generating enough conversation around a book that more people buy it.<\/p>\n“You have Twitch for the gamers, and Etsy for the crafters, and Spotify and SoundCloud for the musicians,” Trowbridge said. “Authors have never had a platform that’s built around their needs, and helping them reach an audience and do it in a way that’s authentic and engaging and can scale, but also creates depth in the relationships.”<\/p>\nAuthors on Copper can host FaceTime-like discussions about their work, which they will be able to sell tickets for in a later version of the app. They can also engage in text-based forum discussions with fans, helping deepen their relationship with their readers. The app will always have a free version for both authors and fans, but later this year, Trowbridge wants to create a premium version of the app, which would offer paying users additional features.<\/p>\nCopper is part of a growing crop of companies that want to help connect authors with readers.
"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/12\/with-sales-momentum-bookshop-org-looks-to-future-in-its-fight-with-amazon\/\">Bookshop.org<\/a>,"https:\/\/libro.fm\/\">Libro.fm<\/a> and"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/21\/folios-24-year-old-founder-is-bootstrapping-a-curated-online-bookstore\/\">Folio<\/a> have offered consumers an alternative to Amazon, while apps like"https:\/\/www.thestorygraph.com\/\">The StoryGraph<\/a> are trying to dethrone the dormant Goodreads.<\/p>\n"attachment_2312608\" style=\"width: 4022px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2312608\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2312608 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/copper-ios-mockups.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"4012\" height=\"2390\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/copper-ios-mockups.png 4012w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/copper-ios-mockups.png?resize=150,89 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/copper-ios-mockups.png?resize=300,179 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/copper-ios-mockups.png?resize=768,458 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/copper-ios-mockups.png?resize=680,405 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/copper-ios-mockups.png?resize=1536,915 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/copper-ios-mockups.png?resize=2048,1220 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/copper-ios-mockups.png?resize=50,30 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 4012px) 100vw, 4012px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2312608\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> Copper<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nThough book sales are"https:\/\/www.authorsguild.org\/industry-advocacy\/book-sales-up-readership-down\/\">increasing<\/a> each year, Trowbridge thinks there hasn’t been meaningful change in the way authors can grow their audience, sell more books and make writing a more sustainable career (if you’re lucky, your self-published book might go viral on TikTok, earn you a book deal and become a New York Times bestseller, but we can’t all be"https:\/\/www.panmacmillan.com\/blogs\/science-fiction-and-fantasy\/tor-uk-acquires-the-atlas-six-fantasy-book-olivie-blake\">Olivie Blake<\/a>).<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nGoodreads, for instance, remains a go-to platform for discovery, but its interface hasn’t visibly changed since"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2013\/03\/28\/amazon-acquires-social-reading-site-goodreads\/\">Amazon bought<\/a> it in 2013. Plus, Trowbridge noted, emerging authors are told to never look at the Goodreads reviews of their books (“You’ll never want to write another book again,” she jokes). It might be a useful platform for readers looking for book recommendations, but it’s not the most author-friendly website. Copper hopes to make a product that’s fun and useful for both readers and writers.<\/p>\n“For authors, you’re not just a writer. You’re kind of a micro-entrepreneur,” Trowbridge told TechCrunch. That statement might repulse some literary types, but promotion is a means to an end — unless if you’re an established superstar, you probably don’t have much help marketing the book you worked so hard on.”Once the book is written, you’re really doing a product launch, and you’re spending six months thinking about how to launch this product and sell it to an engaged audience that’s going to to buy it and read it.”<\/p>\nSo far, Copper has secured $2.5 million in pre-seed funding led by Wave Capital, and including key individual investors like former Time Inc. executive Fran Hauser. Bestselling author and Wharton professor Adam Grant has also been a crucial advisor to the project.<\/p>\nAs Copper launches out of private beta on"https:\/\/apps.apple.com\/us\/app\/copper-books\/id1557778850?utm_source=Marketing+Email&utm_medium=Email&utm_campaign=Copper+Books\">iOS<\/a>, the app has a waitlist of 6,000 potential users, half of whom are published authors. Trowbridge says Copper has had “several hundred” of these authors onboard during private beta.<\/p>\nA primary selling point of Copper is the promise of community, but community can’t exist without enough users. So, Copper will face a moment of truth in the coming months as it charges full-speed ahead in the age-old pursuit of user acquisition.<\/p>\n“Ultimately, we want to build the Instagram for book lovers,” Trowbridge said.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"cvqvfsopfs\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/21\/folios-24-year-old-founder-is-bootstrapping-a-curated-online-bookstore\/\">Folio’s 24-year-old founder is bootstrapping a curated, online bookstore<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; second Apple Store files to hold a union election"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">Apple store employees in Towson, Maryland have"https:\/\/www.goiam.org\/news\/imail\/maryland-apple-store-employees-move-to-join-the-iam\/\">organized a union<\/a> and"https:\/\/www.theverge.com\/2022\/5\/4\/23056187\/apple-second-store-union-election-petition-retail\">petitioned<\/a> to hold an official union election. This marks the third Apple retail location in recent weeks that has taken significant steps toward becoming the first formally recognized Apple union, following stores in"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/18\/apple-union-grand-central\/\">Manhattan<\/a> and"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/21\/apple-store-union-election-atlanta\/\">Atlanta<\/a>.<\/p>\nCalling themselves AppleCORE (Coalition of Organized Retail Employees), the union claims to have the support of the majority of employees at the store and is operating with the support of the International Association of Machinists and Aerospace Workers ("https:\/\/www.goiam.org\/\">IAM<\/a>).<\/p>\n“We have come together as a union because of a deep love of our role as workers within the company and out of care for the company itself,” AppleCORE’s"https:\/\/www.goiam.org\/dear-tim\/\">letter<\/a> to Apple CEO Tim Cook says. “To be clear, the decision to form a union is about us as workers gaining access to rights that we do not currently have.”<\/p>\nAppleCORE hasn’t yet listed specific demands it wants from Apple. Workers at the Atlanta store, represented by the Communications Workers of America, said in a statement that retail workers at Apple have been denied a living wage, cost of living adjustments and equitable stock options.<\/p>\n"https:\/\/fsworkersunited.org\/\">Fruit Stand Workers United<\/a>, the union at the"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/18\/apple-union-grand-central\/\">Grand Central Terminal store<\/a>, is seeking a minimum pay of $30 per hour, more robust benefits including increased tuition reimbursement, more vacation time and better retirement options like higher 401(k) matching.<\/p>\nRight now, Apple retail wages range between $20 and $30 per hour, plus some Apple stock. Apple retail workers also have access to healthcare and tuition reimbursement benefits.<\/p>\nIn order to gain formal recognition, these unions must earn over 50% of votes at an election, orchestrated by the National Labor Relations Board (NLRB). The Atlanta store could be first to unionize, as they’re expected to vote"https:\/\/www.theverge.com\/2022\/5\/3\/23055452\/apple-retail-store-atlanta-union-vote-date-set-june-cwa\">starting June 2<\/a>. As of its announcement to file for an election, over 70% of more than 100 employees at the Atlanta store had indicated support for the union.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"AqSunkFl39\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/18\/apple-union-grand-central\/\">Apple retail workers at the Grand Central store are trying to unionize<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“Apple retail workers at the Grand Central store are trying to unionize” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/18\/apple-union-grand-central\/embed\/#?secret=ndx6LZFigU#?secret=AqSunkFl39\" data-secret=\"AqSunkFl39\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"VbKXGRXhQt\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/21\/apple-store-union-election-atlanta\/\">An Apple Store in Atlanta is the first to file for a union election<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“An Apple Store in Atlanta is the first to file for a union election” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/21\/apple-store-union-election-atlanta\/embed\/#?secret=MQvHokRttY#?secret=VbKXGRXhQt\" data-secret=\"VbKXGRXhQt\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"Apple store employees in Towson, Maryland have organized a union and petitioned to hold an official union election. workers","slug":"retail-workers","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/577012678"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=577012678"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=577012678"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=577012678"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=577012678"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":792407,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/tim-cook\/","name":"Tim Cook","slug":"tim-cook","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/792407"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=792407"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=792407"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=792407"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=792407"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2312009,"date":"2022-05-04T09:04:28","date_gmt":"2022-05-04T16:04:28","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2312009"},"modified":"2022-05-05T10:37:51","modified_gmt":"2022-05-05T17:37:51","slug":"patreon-creator-census-crypto","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/04\/patreon-creator-census-crypto\/","title":{"rendered":"A major Patreon survey shows that most creators don’t want crypto payments"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">Patreon announced the results of its first"https:\/\/blog.patreon.com\/the-first-ever-patreon-creator-census\">creator census<\/a>, which invited the community to share feedback about how the fan membership platform can best support independent creatives. Out of 250,000 creators active on Patreon, over 13,000 people responded to the survey, representing 113 countries and 18 languages.<\/p>\nAccording to the survey, video is the most popular primary medium on Patreon, representing 38% of respondents. The next most popular categories are writing (17%) and podcasting (14%). Fifty-six percent of Patreon creators consider themselves closer to being seasoned professionals, while 44% say they’re closer to just starting out. Interestingly enough, respondents also said that over 40% of their creative income came from Patreon.<\/p>\n"attachment_2312030\" style=\"width: 1272px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2312030\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2312030 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-11.29.12-AM.png\" alt=\"A graph showing that creators make 41% of their income on Patreon\" width=\"1262\" height=\"996\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-11.29.12-AM.png 1262w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-11.29.12-AM.png?resize=150,118 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-11.29.12-AM.png?resize=300,237 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-11.29.12-AM.png?resize=768,606 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-11.29.12-AM.png?resize=680,537 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-11.29.12-AM.png?resize=50,39 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1262px) 100vw, 1262px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2312030\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> Patreon<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nLinktree, the link-in-bio monetization platform, also recently"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/20\/linktree-creator-economy-report-research\/\">conducted a survey<\/a> of 9,500 creators. Both Linktree and Patreon reported that brand sponsorships don’t make up as much of creator earnings as we"https:\/\/neoreach.com\/creator-earnings\/\">previously thought<\/a> — Linktree said that 70% of creators earn less than 10% of their earnings from brand deals, while Patreon creators reported that this makes up 2% of their income. Still, these results could be skewed since it’s a holistic report of creators from all genres. Tours and live shows are a huge part of musicians’ income, for example, but Patreon’s data says it makes up just 2% of creators’ income. That’s probably because musicians don’t make up a large portion of Patreon creators (plus, touring hasn’t been too feasible over the last few years because \u2026 you know).<\/p>\nPatreon also surveyed creators about their priorities for future Patreon products. Over the last several months, Patreon executives like CEO Jack Conte and CPO Julian Gutman have said that the company"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/10\/29\/patreon-confirms-its-exploring-crypto-as-a-way-for-creators-to-make-money\/\">has been interested<\/a> in exploring whether crypto tools could help creators make money. Through its Creator Policy Engagement Program, Patreon even"https:\/\/blog.patreon.com\/fall-2021-creator-policy-engagement-update\"> floated the idea<\/a> of creator coins as an avenue for monetization. Gutman"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/21\/patreon-cpo-interview-double-in-size-2022\/\">told TechCrunch<\/a> in December that the company had considered building a small crypto team to examine potential options, but that there weren’t any plans set in stone for a plunge into web3.<\/p>\n\u201cIt\u2019s not, \u2018Hey, let\u2019s go build an NFT platform right now,\u2019 but you know, a couple of folks that are focused on this full time,\u201d Gutman"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/21\/patreon-cpo-interview-double-in-size-2022\/\">said at the time<\/a>. \u201cAnd by the way, they might conclude, \u2018Hey, you know what, there\u2019s nothing for us to build here right now,\u2019 which is a totally fine, reasonable conclusion.\u201d<\/p>\nBut feedback from the creator census showed that 43% of creators are strongly against crypto payments, while 30% said they don’t care. Nine percent said crypto payments would be crucial, while 18% said they would be nice to have.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n"attachment_2312055\" style=\"width: 1254px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2312055\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2312055 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-11.48.17-AM.png\" alt=\"A graph showing respondent interest in crypto payments \" width=\"1244\" height=\"868\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-11.48.17-AM.png 1244w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-11.48.17-AM.png?resize=150,105 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-11.48.17-AM.png?resize=300,209 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-11.48.17-AM.png?resize=768,536 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-11.48.17-AM.png?resize=680,474 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-11.48.17-AM.png?resize=50,35 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1244px) 100vw, 1244px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2312055\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> Patreon<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n“Some creators, including many who took this survey, are opposed to Patreon building any web3 functionality due to concerns about potential fraudulent behavior, environmental sustainability and inaccessibility of the technology in its present applications,” the census report said. “Other creators already offer web3 benefits off Patreon and are excited about the flexibility and value they can offer memberships with new types of digital goods.”<\/p>\nSure, crypto skeptics could simply just not use web3 features with their audience. But some creators worry that their audience will be less likely to support them via Patreon if the company dabbles in web3.<\/p>\n\u201cAny creator becomes like customer service and a representative for any of the services that you use,”"http:\/\/multitude.productions\">Multitude Productions<\/a> CEO Amanda McLoughlin"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/30\/not-every-creator-economy-startup-is-built-for-creators\/\">told TechCrunch<\/a> last year, noting that patrons had reached out to her in the past with concerns about Patreon pivoting to crypto. For small business owners that make a significant chunk of their income from fan memberships on Patreon, these seemingly small feature updates can make a serious impact.<\/p>\n“Our focus continues to be on how to give creators more ownership and leverage over their content, and that includes exploring the benefits of web3 technologies,” Patreon said in an email to TechCrunch. “However, neither our creators nor Patreon are prioritizing this space right now.”<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"J6yzJqNsiC\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/30\/not-every-creator-economy-startup-is-built-for-creators\/\">Not every creator economy startup is built for creators<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; Company’s\u00a0"https:\/\/nytco-assets.nytimes.com\/2022\/05\/NYT-Press-Release-3.27.2022-Final-O2ACvs2.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">first-quarter financial results<\/a> prove what we’ve all known all along: people really like"https:\/\/www.nytimes.com\/games\/wordle\/index.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Wordle<\/a>.<\/p>\nYou know the story by now. Josh Wardle made a fun little word game for his partner, shared it with some friends (who happened to be some influential tech people, since Wardle has worked at places like Reddit and MSCHF), who shared it with some more friends, and eventually it was all anyone with an internet connection could talk about.<\/p>\nAt first, Wardle wasn’t trying to profit off his ad-free, lightweight word game. But being solely responsible for a viral word game is a big commitment, so at the end of January, he"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/31\/popular-puzzle-game-wordle-is-being-purchased-by-the-new-york-times\/\">sold the game to The New York Times<\/a> for an undisclosed amount in the “low seven figures.”<\/p>\n\u201cIf you\u2019ve followed along with the story of Wordle, you\u2019ll know that NYT games play a big part in its origins and so this step feels very natural to me,” Wardle said in a"https:\/\/twitter.com\/powerlanguish\/status\/1488263944309731329\">tweet<\/a>. “When the game moves to the NYT site, it will be free to play for everyone, and I am working with them to make sure your wins and streaks will be preserved.\u201d<\/p>\nAbout three months after Wordle’s sale to The New York Times, the paper"https:\/\/nytco-assets.nytimes.com\/2022\/05\/NYT-Press-Release-3.27.2022-Final-O2ACvs2.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">announced<\/a> that the game brought “an unprecedented tens of millions of new users to The Times.” This drove the company’s best quarter ever for net subscriber additions to Games. Even though Wordle remains free, The New York Times has been covertly advertising its other games like Spelling Bee through Wordle. A subscription to New York Times Games costs $5 per month, or $40 per year.<\/p>\nWhen Wardle spoke to TechCrunch weeks before the acquisition, he noted that New York Times Games served as an inspiration for the game. Unlike past viral games — think"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2014\/02\/01\/developer-behind-flappy-bird-the-impossible-game-blowing-up-the-app-store-says-he-just-got-lucky\/\">Flappy Bird<\/a> — the game isn’t addicting, as you cannot play more than once each day. That game design is intentional.<\/p>\n“My partner and I play a lot of The New York Times word games, and they follow that one-a-day model,” he"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/12\/josh-wardle-interview-wordle\/\">told TechCrunch<\/a>.<\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\nAlso similar to The Times, Wordle forges a sense of community among players, since everyone is solving the same puzzle. Wardle added, “One thing that is interesting to reflect on, though, is that Wordle could be one a day, but if everybody was getting a different word on that day \u2014 if the word was random but you could still only play one \u2014 it wouldn\u2019t have caught on the way it has.”<\/p>\nBut perhaps what propelled Wordle to an unexpected level of virality is the ease of sharing your Wordle results emoji grid.<\/p>\nPeople share their Wordle results in WhatsApp chats, Facebook posts and texts to their mom, but Twitter played a significant role in its popularity too.<\/p>\nTwitter data scientist Lauren Fratamico published a"https:\/\/blog.twitter.com\/engineering\/en_us\/topics\/insights\/2022\/understanding-twitter-conversations--a-wordle-case-study\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">case study<\/a> yesterday examining how Wordle spread on the platform over time.<\/p>\n"attachment_2311977\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2311977\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2311977\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-10.44.17-AM.png?w=680\" alt=\"A graph showing the growth of Wordle on Twitter -- it peaks in January\" width=\"680\" height=\"352\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-10.44.17-AM.png 1416w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-10.44.17-AM.png?resize=300,155 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-10.44.17-AM.png?resize=768,397 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-10.44.17-AM.png?resize=680,352 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-10.44.17-AM.png?resize=50,26 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2311977\" rel=\"noopener\">Twitter"screen-reader-text\">(opens in a new window)<\/span><\/a><\/p><\/div><\/p>\nThe study revealed that 3.3 million people have tweeted about Wordle since mid-October for a total of 32.2 million tweets. Tweets about Wordle have earned over 6.6 trillion views, 58 million likes and 9 million replies.<\/p>\nAt its peak popularity, there were 500,000 tweets about Wordle per day — but, this peak in late January coincides with The New York Times’ purchase of the game, which certainly contributed to the discourse. Even though there’s a downward trend in tweets about Wordle (now, it’s about 200,000 per day), that doesn’t necessarily mean people aren’t playing as much. Rather, maybe it became a bit"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/31\/cheugiest-tech-moments-of-2021\/\">cheugy<\/a> to share your scores every day.<\/p>\n“One thing I will say is that the majority of players are not actually posting their results on Twitter,” Wardle told TechCrunch in January. “There\u2019s an account called"https:\/\/twitter.com\/WordleStats\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Wordle Stats<\/a> that looks at Twitter, then collects all the grids people share, then posts it the next day and says, ‘Okay, 30% of people got it in four,’ and I think it was two days ago that it collected 100,000-something, whereas at that time, close to 2 million people played Wordle.”<\/p>\nIn case you’re wondering, according to the sample size of people who posted Wordle results on Twitter, the hardest word was SWILL (2\/19\/22), which took tweeters an average of 4.88 guesses to solve. The easiest was PLANT (4\/22\/22), which was solved on average in 3.32 guesses.<\/p>\n"attachment_2311989\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2311989\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2311989\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-10.54.10-AM.png?w=680\" alt=\"A graph showing what percentage of guesses it takes for people to solve a wordle -- the highest percentage is 4 guesses\" width=\"680\" height=\"331\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-10.54.10-AM.png 1456w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-10.54.10-AM.png?resize=150,73 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-10.54.10-AM.png?resize=300,146 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-10.54.10-AM.png?resize=768,373 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-10.54.10-AM.png?resize=680,331 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-04-at-10.54.10-AM.png?resize=50,24 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2311989\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong>"https:\/\/blog.twitter.com\/engineering\/en_us\/topics\/insights\/2022\/understanding-twitter-conversations--a-wordle-case-study\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Twitter"screen-reader-text\">(opens in a new window)<\/span><\/a><\/p><\/div><\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"7J1AJMoWBq\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/12\/josh-wardle-interview-wordle\/\">Wordle founder Josh Wardle on going viral and what comes next<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; Circle, a ‘Close Friends’-like feature, is testing"},"content":{"rendered":""speakable-summary\">Twitter Circle, the app’s spin on an Instagram-like “Close Friends” feature, is finally testing.
"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/01\/twitter-considers-new-features-for-tweeting-only-to-friends-under-different-personas-and-more\/\">\u00a0<\/a>The feature was teased as one of many potential product updates"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/01\/twitter-considers-new-features-for-tweeting-only-to-friends-under-different-personas-and-more\/\">in July<\/a>, and last month, it"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/16\/twitters-spin-on-the-close-friends-story-might-be-on-its-way-soon\/\">cropped up live on the site<\/a> due to a bug. Now, a small number of users can shitpost to their 150 closest friends as the feature enters a live testing phase.<\/p>\n"attachment_2311370\" style=\"width: 1210px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">"caption-attachment-2311370\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2311370 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-03-at-2.05.16-PM.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1200\" height=\"948\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-03-at-2.05.16-PM.png 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-03-at-2.05.16-PM.png?resize=150,119 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-03-at-2.05.16-PM.png?resize=300,237 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-03-at-2.05.16-PM.png?resize=768,607 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-03-at-2.05.16-PM.png?resize=680,537 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/05\/Screen-Shot-2022-05-03-at-2.05.16-PM.png?resize=50,40 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1200px) 100vw, 1200px\" \/>"caption-attachment-2311370\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits:<\/strong> Screenshot by TechCrunch<\/p><\/div><\/p>\nTwitter says that the feature is in its early stages, which is why only some users have access. Even if you yourself can’t make a Twitter Circle, you can see tweets from users who do have the feature, so long as you’re in their Circle, of course. When you build your Circle, Twitter will recommend that you add mutuals that you interact with often (odds are, those people might be your close friends). You can add people who aren’t following you, but they probably won’t see your tweet since \u2026 they aren’t following you.<\/p>\nWhen you reply to a tweet that someone sent out to their Circle, other members of the Circle can see your response and interact with it (unless if you’re on private).<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Some Tweets are for everyone & others are just for people you\u2019ve picked.<\/p>\nWe\u2019re now testing Twitter Circle, which lets you add up to 150 people who can see your Tweets when you want to share with a smaller crowd. <\/p>\nSome of you can create your own Twitter Circle beginning today!"https:\/\/t.co\/nLaTG8qctp\">pic.twitter.com\/nLaTG8qctp<\/a><\/p>"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n— Twitter Safety (@TwitterSafety)"https:\/\/twitter.com\/TwitterSafety\/status\/1521540727557218309?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">May 3, 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\nWhen you add or remove people from your Twitter Circle, they won’t know, so don’t worry about accidentally sending out awkward notifications. Unlike Google+ Circles ("https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/10\/08\/looking-back-at-google\/\">RIP<\/a>), you only get one Circle, so choose its purpose wisely.<\/p>\nTo tweet to your Circle, click the oval above the text box when you’re writing a tweet, then change the audience from “Everyone” to “Twitter Circle,” the same way you would tweet to a"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/08\/twitter-communities\/\">Community<\/a>.<\/p>\nWe can only hope Elon Musk understands that"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/27\/judge-quashes-elon-musks-attempt-to-end-sec-settlement-over-tesla-tweets\/\">SEC regulations<\/a> apply to Twitter Circle tweets, too.<\/p>\n"embed breakout\">\n"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"qvQU09bQfA\">"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/16\/twitters-spin-on-the-close-friends-story-might-be-on-its-way-soon\/\">Twitter’s spin on the close friends story might be on its way soon<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"“Twitter’s spin on the close friends story might be on its way soon” — TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/16\/twitters-spin-on-the-close-friends-story-might-be-on-its-way-soon\/embed\/#?secret=tZTVEoebD3#?secret=qvQU09bQfA\" data-secret=\"qvQU09bQfA\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"Twitter Circle, the app’s spin on an Instagram-like “Close Friends” feature, is finally testing.\u00a0The feature was teased as one of many potential product updates in July, and last month, it cropped up live on the site due to a bug.
